Woman's Capacity to Serve as Judge in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling and dispute on woman's judicial authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on women judges, identify the disputed areas with the Shafi'i school, and apply the analogy between judgment and testimony to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A woman may judge all cases except fixed punishments and retaliation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary presents a nuanced Hanafi ruling on women's judicial authority. While the Hanafi school permits women to serve as judges in most matters, it restricts them from presiding over hadd (fixed corporal punishments) and qisas (retaliation) cases. The ruling is built on an analogy to women's testimony, which is accepted in financial matters but not in hudud and qisas. The passage also addresses the Shafi'i objection and clarifies that the guardian who appoints a woman judge incurs sin, yet her judgments remain valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
First, extract the core Hanafi position: a woman may judge in all cases except hadd and qisas. Note that her judgment is valid (sahih) but her guardian (mawliha) is sinful for appointing her.
The ruling is based on the principle that judgment follows testimony.
2
Examine the analogical proof (qiyas)
The passage states 'al-qada ka al-shahada' (judgment is like testimony). Since a woman's testimony is accepted in non-hadd and non-qisas matters, her judgment is similarly accepted. This is a qiyas with zanni thubut and dalala.
This analogy is the primary Hanafi proof.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that women have deficient intellect ('qasr aql') and thus cannot hold judicial authority. The Hanafi response clarifies that this deficiency does not negate all legal capacity; women serve as witnesses, supervisors of waqf, and executors, proving their capacity in certain domains.
The response highlights partial capacity, not total incapacity.
4
Explore the exceptions and consensus
If a woman judges in hadd or qisas and another judge who deems it permissible ratifies the judgment, it is enforced by consensus (ijma). Al-Nasafi adds that even if the judgment itself involved disputed evidence (e.g., women's testimony in hadd), it is enforceable.
This shows the respect for ijtihad and prevents annulment by other judges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقضي المرأة في غير حدّ وقود [ أي قصاص؛ لأن القضاء كالشهادة، وشهادتها جائزة في غيرهما فكذا يجوز قضاؤها في غيرهما. (عيني)] لما مر من أهل قضاء أهل الشهادة وشهادة المرأة جائزة في غير الحد والقصاص، فكذا قضاؤها إلا أن موليها آثم لخبر خاب قوم ولوا أمرهم امرأة ، وعن الشافعي أنه لا يجوز أن تولي المرأة؛ لقصور عقلها بإخبار الشارع، قلنا: نقصان عقلها لا يفيد سلب أهليتها بالكلية ألا ترى أنها تصلح شاهدة وناظرة في الأوقاف ووصية على اليتامى وقال الإمام العتابي امرأة قلدت القضاء، وقضت في الأموال صح؛ لأنها تصلح شاهدة في باب الأموال، فتصلح قاضية فيها، ولو قضت بالحدود والقصاص، وأمضاه قاض آخر يرى جوازه، نفذ بالإجماع؛ لأن نفس القضاء مجتهد فيه، فإن شريحاً كان يجوز شهادة النساء مع رجل في الحدود والقصاص، وقال الشيخ أبو الحسين النسفي: ولو قضى القاضي في الحدود والقصاص بشهادة رجل وامرأتين نفذ قضاؤه، وليس لغيره إبطاله؛ لأنه قضى في فصل مجتهد فيه، وليس نفس القضاء هنا مختلفاً فيه. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢٥/٢] (فتح)
And a woman judges in other than prescribed punishment and retaliation [i.e., qisas; because judgment is like testimony, and her testimony is permissible in other than them, so similarly her judgment is permissible in other than them. (Ayni)] Due to the principle that judgment follows the domain of testimony, and a woman's testimony is permissible in other than hadd and qisas, so similarly her judgment. However, her guardian is sinful due to the hadith: 'A people who entrust their affairs to a woman will not succeed.' And from al-Shafi'i that it is not permissible to appoint a woman due to deficiency of her intellect, as reported by the Lawgiver. We say: Deficiency of her intellect does not negate her legal capacity entirely; do you not see that she is qualified as a witness, supervisor of endowments, and executor for orphans? And Imam al-Attabi said: A woman who was appointed judge and judged in property matters is valid because she is qualified as a witness in property matters, so she is qualified as a judge therein. And if she judged in hadd and qisas, and another judge who deems it permissible ratified it, it is enforced by consensus because the judgment itself is a matter of ijtihad. Indeed, Shuraih used to permit women's testimony with a man in hadd and qisas. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Nasafi said: If a judge judged in hadd and qisas based on the testimony of one man and two women, his judgment is enforced, and no one else may annul it because he judged in a matter of ijtihad, and the judgment itself is not disputed here. (Fath).
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage presents both the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i objection regarding women judges. The Hanafi ruling is that a woman may serve as judge in all cases except hadd (fixed corporal punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The reasoning is analogical: since judgment is similar to testimony, and a woman's testimony is accepted in financial and other matters but not in hadd and qisas, the same applies to her judicial authority. However, the guardian who appoints her sins due to the hadith warning against entrusting affairs to women. Shafi'i argues total prohibition based on women's intellectual deficiency as per divine texts. The Hanafi response clarifies that deficiency does not remove all legal capacity; women serve as witnesses, supervisors of waqf, and executors, proving their eligibility in certain domains. Al-Attabi affirms validity for property cases. Importantly, if a woman does judge in hadd or qisas and another judge ratifies it, the judgment stands because the matter is one of ijtihad. Al-Nasafi extends this: even if the judgment itself involved disputed evidence (e.g., women's testimony in hadd), it is enforceable and cannot be overturned by another judge, as ijtihad permits such variation.

Key Terms
حدّ (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by divine law (e.g., for theft, adultery).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, specifically equal punishment for bodily harm or death.
موليها (mawliha): Her guardian (the one who appoints her as judge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only cases involving testimony of two women

Key Takeaway
A woman may judge all cases except fixed punishments (hadd) and retaliation (qisas); her judgment is valid, but her guardian incurs sin for appointing her.

Delegation of Judicial Authority
Ruling on delegation of judicial authority with proof by analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge delegating another judge, explain the Qiyas proof, and identify the conditions for valid ratification.

Core Idea
A judge cannot delegate another to judge unless the ruler authorizes it; any delegation without permission is like an agent exceeding authority.

In Islamic judiciary, a judge's authority is personal and non-delegable unless the ruler explicitly grants the power of delegation. This lesson examines the ruling on istikhlaf (delegation) and the conditions under which a delegated judgment may still be valid through ratification. The analogy to agency (wakalah) forms the core proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The passage states that a judge does not delegate (la yastakhlif). Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the default hukm is: it is not permissible (la yajuz) even with an excuse.
The default is prohibition without authorization.
2
Locate the dalil and its form
The author uses a Qiyas (analogy): the judge is like an agent (wakil). An agent cannot delegate without the principal's permission. Identify the asl (agency), far' (judge), and illah (limited authority).
The illah is that both have a restricted mandate.
3
Understand the exceptions and ratification
If the judge delegates without permission but the delegatee judges in his presence, or outside his presence but the judge ratifies it, the judgment becomes valid. This mirrors the rule for an agent who acts without permission but is later ratified.
Ratification (ijazah) retroactively validates.
4
List the conditions for valid ratification
The delegatee must be qualified (ahlan): free, not flogged for qadhf, Muslim. If any condition is missing, ratification is ineffective.
These are the minimal qualifications for a judge in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Distinguish the Friday prayer exception
The text contrasts the case of a person ordered to lead Friday prayer: he may delegate without permission because it is time-bound. Understand why this exception exists and how it differs from judicial delegation.
The exception is due to necessity (darurah) to preserve the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يستخلف : [ أي لا يجوز الاستخلاف على القضاء. (ط، عيني)] ولو بعذر؛ لأنه مفوض إليه القضاء دون التقليد، فصار كالوكيل بالبيع أو النكاح ليس له أن يوكل إلا بإذن الموكل أو التفويض، فلو استخلف من لم يفوض إليه ذلك، فقضى الثاني بمحضر من الأول، أو بغير محضره، إلا أنه أجازه، جاز كالوكيل إذا وكل مع عدم الإذن بشرط أن يكون الثاني أهلاً للقضاء لا رقيقاً ولا محدوداً في قذف ولا كافراً، فإن لم يكن أهلاً لم يجز، - بخلاف المأمور بالجمعة، وإذا رفع إليه حكم قاض قبله أمضاه
And he does not delegate [i.e., it is not permissible to delegate judicial authority. (T, Ayni)] even with an excuse; because he is entrusted with judging but not with delegation (taqlid), so he becomes like an agent for sale or marriage who may not appoint a sub-agent except with permission of the principal or authorization. If he delegated to one to whom that was not authorized, and the second judged in the presence of the first, or not in his presence but he ratified it, it is permissible, like an agent who appoints a sub-agent without permission, on condition that the second is qualified for judging: not a slave, not one who has been flogged for false accusation (qadhf), and not a disbeliever. If he is not qualified, it is not permissible. Different is the one ordered to perform Friday prayer (Jumu'ah). And when a judgment of a previous judge is presented to him, he enforces it.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage establishes the general principle that a judge (qadi) may not delegate another person to act as judge in his place, even with a valid excuse, unless the delegating authority (the caliph or sultan) has expressly authorized him to do so. The reasoning is analogical: the judge is like an agent (wakil) appointed for a specific task (judging), and an agent cannot appoint another agent (tawkil) without explicit permission from the principal (muwwakil). If the judge nevertheless delegates and the delegatee (the second judge) judges in the presence of the first judge, or even outside his presence but the first judge subsequently ratifies the judgment, then the judgment is valid – but only if the delegatee is legally qualified (ahlan): not a slave, not one who has been punished for false accusation of adultery (hadd al-qadhf), and not a disbeliever. If the delegatee lacks any of these qualifications, the judgment is invalid. An exception is mentioned for Friday prayer (Jumu'ah): the imam appointed to lead Jumu'ah may delegate someone else to lead in his place even without explicit authorization, because Jumu'ah is time-bound (mawqut) and may lapse if the imam is unable. The passage concludes by transitioning to the next ruling: when a judgment of a previous judge is presented to the current judge, he must enforce it, subject to the conditions in the next lesson.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The act of a judge appointing another to act as judge in his place.
مفوض إليه القضاء (mufawwad ilayhi al-qada): One who is entrusted with judging but not with the power of delegation (taqlid).
أهل للقضاء (ahl li al-qada): Qualified for judging: free, not punished for qadhf, Muslim, sane, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever he has a valid excuse
B) Only if the delegating authority (caliph) has authorized him in writing
C) Only if the delegatee is present in his court
D) Never, delegation is always invalid

Key Takeaway
A judge may not delegate another to judge without the ruler's authorization; any delegation is void unless ratified and the delegatee is qualified.

Enforcement of Prior Judgment
Conditions for enforcing a previous judge's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a subsequent judge must enforce a prior judgment and identify when a judgment may be overturned due to contradiction with definitive texts.

Core Idea
A prior judgment is enforced in ijtihad matters unless it contradicts qat'i proofs or ijma.

In the Hanafi judicial system, finality and stability of judgments are paramount. However, a subsequent judge is not bound to enforce a prior judgment if it conflicts with the Quran, the well-known Sunnah, or consensus of the early generations. This lesson examines the limits of judicial deference and the conditions for overturning a prior ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The default rule: when a prior judge's ruling is presented, the subsequent judge enforces it regardless of his own opinion or the prior judge's status. This is derived from the indefinite phrasing in the Arabic text.
The rule applies to all prior judgments unless an exception is proven.
2
Identify the exceptions
The ruling is not enforced if it contradicts the Book (Quran), the well-known Sunnah (al-sunnah al-mashhura), or ijma (consensus). Each exception is explained with examples.
Contradiction of qat'i al-dalala texts is kufr, not mere error.
3
Understand the scope of 'ijtihad'
Matters of ijtihad (where jurists differ based on valid proofs) are enforceable. The second judge's ijtihad is equal to the first's, so he cannot reverse it just because he disagrees.
The underlying reason: both ijtihads are equally probable.
4
Note the condition of knowledge
According to al-Jami' al-Saghir, the second judge must be aware of the scholarly disagreement. If he is ignorant, his enforcement may be invalid.
This is an intra-Hanafi condition, not universally accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا رفع إليه حكم قاض قبله أمضاه : [ أي أمضى القاضي المرفوع إليه حكم القاضي الآخر. (مع، فتح)] أي حكم بمقتضاه، وافق ذلك الحكم رأيه أو خالفه بقي الآخر على قضائه أو مات أو عزل؛ لأنه نكرة في سياق الشرط، فيعم، وقوله: "إن لم يخالف الكتاب" أي الحكم الذي لم يختلف في تأويله السلف كالقضاء بحل مزنية أبيه أو ابنه أو بصحة نكاح أم مزنية أو بنتها، ولابد من تقييد الكتاب بأن لا يكون قطعي الدلالة، وإلا فمخالفة المتواتر من كتاب أو سنة إذا كان قطعي الدلالة كفر ، وقوله "والسنة المشهورة" كتحليل المطلقة الثلاث للزوج الأول بلا وطء الزوج الثاني؛ لأنه مخالف لحديث العسيلة، وكالقضاء بشاهد ويمين فإنه مخالف للحديث المشهور: "البينة على المدعي، واليمين على من أنكر"، وقيد بالمشهورة؛ احترازاً عن الحديث الغريب. وقوله: "والإجماع" أي الذي ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي، وغير المستند إليه يسمى خلافاً لا اختلافاً، والمعتبر: الاختلاف في الصدر الأول، ونظير مخالفة الإجماع: كما إذا قضى بجواز بيع أم الولد، فللقاضي الثاني أن ينقضه؛ لأنه مخالف لإجماع التابعين، والأصل في إمضاء القاضي ما رفع إليه إذا لم يكن مخالفاً للأدلة المذكورة: أن القضاء متى لاقى محلاً مجتهداً فيه ينفذ، ولا يرده غيره؛ لأن اجتهاد الثاني كاجتهاد الأول في أن كلاً منهما يحتمل الأول باتصال القضاء به، فلا ينتقض بما هو دونه درجة، وهو ما لم يتصل القضاء به، وفي "الجامع الصغير": وما اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى به القاضي، ثم جاء القاضي الآخر يرى غير ذلك، أمضاه، وقالوا: شرطه: أن يكون عالماً باختلاف العلماء، حتى لو قضى في فصل مجتهد فيه، وهو لا يعلم بذلك، لا يجوز قضاؤه عند عامتهم. (عيني، عناية، فتح) الخطأ، وقد رجح
And when a judgment of a previous judge is presented to him, he enforces it [i.e., the judge to whom the judgment is presented enforces the judgment of the other judge. (Ma, Fath)] meaning he judges according to it, whether he agrees with that judgment or disagrees, whether the other judge remains in his position or dies or is dismissed; because it is indefinite in the context of condition, so it is general. And his statement: 'provided it does not contradict the Book' i.e., the judgment regarding which the predecessors (salaf) did not differ in interpretation, such as a judgment permitting marriage with one's adulterous father's daughter or marriage of one's adulterous mother or daughter. It is necessary to restrict 'the Book' to that which is not qat'i al-dalala (decisive in meaning); otherwise, contradicting the mutawatir from Book or Sunnah if qat'i al-dalala is kufr. And his statement 'and the well-known Sunnah' such as making a triple divorced woman lawful for the first husband without intercourse with the second husband; because it contradicts the hadith of 'asila (honey)?, and like judging based on one witness and an oath, which contradicts the well-known hadith: 'Evidence is on the plaintiff, and the oath is on the one who denies.' He restricted to 'well-known' to exclude the rare (gharib) hadith. And his statement 'and ijma' i.e., that in which there is no dissent based on a legal proof; that which is not so based is called dissent (khilaf) not disagreement (ikhtilaf). The considered ikhtilaf is that of the early generation (sadr al-awwal). An example of contradicting ijma: like if he judged that it is permissible to sell an umm al-walad, the second judge may overturn it because it contradicts the consensus of the Successors (tabi'in). The principle regarding enforcement of what is presented to the judge, if it does not contradict the mentioned proofs: that when a judgment meets a matter of ijtihad, it is enforced and no one else may return it, because the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, in that each of them is probable; the first is connected to the judgment, so it is not invalidated by what is of a lower degree, i.e., that which is not connected. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Whatever the jurists differed upon, if a judge judged it, then another judge who holds a different opinion comes, he enforces it.' They said: its condition is that he be knowledgeable of the disagreement of the scholars; so if he judged in a matter of ijtihad without knowing that, his judgment is not permissible according to most of them. (Ayni, Inayah, Fath) ... error, and he preponderated...
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage lays out the principle that a subsequent judge must enforce the judgment of a prior judge, provided the judgment does not contradict clear texts: the Book (Quran), the well-known Sunnah (al-sunnah al-mashhura), or consensus (ijma). The condition 'does not contradict the Book' is explained: it refers to cases where the interpretation (ta'wil) is not decisively contradicted by the salaf. For example, a judgment permitting marriage with one's own child from adultery is such a case. But if the judgment contradicts a qat'i al-dalala text (decisive meaning), it is kufr, not mere error. Similarly, contradicting the well-known Sunnah, like allowing a triple divorced woman to remarry her first husband without intercourse with the second (contradicting the hadith of 'asila), or judging based on one witness and an oath (contradicting the famous hadith 'al-bayyinatu 'ala al-mudda'i'), would invalidate the judgment. The passage distinguishes well-known hadith from rare ones (gharib). Ijma (consensus) here means consensus based on a legal proof; a minority dissent (khilaf) based on a proof does not invalidate the consensus. The example of selling umm al-walad is given: since the Successors (tabi'in) had consensus that such sale is not allowed (umm al-walad becomes free upon master's death), a judgment permitting it can be overturned. The underlying principle is that whenever a judgment concerns a matter of ijtihad (a disputed issue among scholars), it is enforceable and cannot be reversed by another judge, because both judges exercise ijtihad and each opinion is equally probable. However, there is a condition: the second judge must be aware of the disagreement among scholars. If he ruled in an ijtihad matter without knowing it was disputed, his judgment is not valid according to most scholars. The passage ends with an apparent reference to an error and a preponderated view, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
السنة المشهورة (al-sunnah al-mashhura): A well-known hadith transmitted by a sufficient number to be considered reliable (but not necessarily mutawatir).
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah on a ruling.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent legal reasoning by a qualified scholar to derive a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default rule regarding enforcement of a prior judge's ruling in the Hanafi school?
A) It is always enforced unless the subsequent judge has a stronger ijtihad.
B) It is enforced unless it contradicts the Quran, well-known Sunnah, or ijma.
C) It is enforced only if the subsequent judge agrees with it.
D) It is never enforced; each case is judged anew.

Key Takeaway
A prior judgment must be enforced by a subsequent judge unless it clearly contradicts the Quran, well-known Sunnah, or consensus of the early generations.

Judge's Authority to Appoint a Deputy
Ruling on the judge's power to appoint deputies with or without Imam's permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when a judge may appoint a deputy in Hanafi fiqh, differentiating between cases with and without the Imam's delegation, and apply the analogy to agency (wakalah).

Core Idea
A judge can only appoint a deputy with the Imam's delegation, except for Jumu'ah due to time sensitivity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the judge's authority to appoint deputies (istikhlaf). It establishes a general rule that such authority requires delegation from the Imam, drawing an analogy to the principal-agent relationship. However, it also introduces an exception for the Jumu'ah prayer, where necessity overrides the standard requirement due to the time-bound nature of the prayer. By studying this lesson, you will understand the conditions under which a judge may delegate judicial duties and the legal reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
The judge may appoint a deputy only if the Imam has delegated the authority, explicitly or implicitly (e.g., by saying 'Appoint whomever you wish').
Explicit delegation is clear; implicit delegation arises from titles like 'Judge of Judges'.
2
Understand the Analogy (Qiyas) to Agency
The judge's authority is analogous to an agent (wakil) who can appoint sub-agents with the principal's permission. The sub-agent becomes the principal's agent, and the first agent cannot dismiss him. Similarly, the deputy judge becomes the Imam's agent.
The text contrasts this with an executor (wasi) who has inherent power to appoint and dismiss.
3
Examine the Exception for Jumu'ah
Despite lacking delegation, the judge for Jumu'ah can appoint a deputy because the prayer is time-sensitive and at risk of being missed. This is allowed by istihsan (juristic preference).
The text states: 'يجوز له أن يستخلف غيره، وإن لم يأذن له الإمام بالاستخلاف'.
4
Analyze Nuances for Jumu'ah
If the Imam dies before the Jumu'ah prayer begins, the deputy must have attended the sermon; if the prayer has started, the deputy need not have attended. This is because the sermon is a condition for commencement, not for continuation.
The distinction is based on the ruling that the deputy begins anew (المستخلف بان لا مفتتح).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فوض إليه الإمام أن يستخلف بأن قال له: ولّ من شئت، له أن يولي من شاء، ويصير نائباً عن الإمام في التولية حتى لا يملك عزله كالوكيل إذا أذن له الموكل بالتوكيل، فوكل، فصار الثاني وكيلاً عن الموكل حتى لا يملك الوكيل الأول عزله، ولا ينعزل النائب بموته، وينعزلان بموت الموكل، بخلاف الوصي حيث يملك الإيصاء إلى غيره ويملك التوكيل والعزل في حياته، ولو فوض إليه الإمام العزل بأن قال له استبدل من شئت، كان له العزل؛ لأنه ملكه بالتفويض سواء كان التفويض صريحاً كما مر، أو دلالة مثل أن يقول الإمام: جعلتك قاضي القضاة، فإن الذي يتصرف فيهم تقليداً وعزلاً. (عيني، فتح) هو القضاة قاضي بخلاف أي بإقامتها، حيث يجوز له أن يستخلف غيره، وإن لم يأذن له الإمام بالاستخلاف؛ لكونها على شرف الفوات؛ لأنها مؤقتة بوقت يفوت الأداء بانقضائه، وليس القضاء كالجمعة؛ لأنه غير مؤقت بوقت، ثم إذا حدث الإمام قبل أن يشرع في الجمعة، لم يجز له أن يستخلف إلا من شهد الخطبة؛ لأن الخطبة شرط فيها، فلا تنعقد دونها، وإن كان شرع فيها جاز له أن يستخلف من لم يشهد الخطبة؛ لأن المستخلف بان لا مفتتح، والخطبة من شرائط افتتاح الجمعة. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
If the Imam delegated to him the authority to appoint a deputy by saying to him 'Appoint whomever you wish', he has the right to appoint whomever he wishes, and he becomes a deputy of the Imam in the appointment so that he does not have the power to dismiss him, like an agent when the principal gives him permission to appoint a sub-agent, and he appoints, so the second becomes an agent of the principal so that the first agent does not have the power to dismiss him, and the deputy is not dismissed by the death of the Imam, but both are dismissed by the death of the principal, unlike the executor (wasi) who has the power to appoint a successor and has the power to appoint and dismiss during his lifetime. And if the Imam delegated to him the authority to dismiss by saying 'Replace whomever you wish', he has the right to dismiss because he owned the power by delegation, whether the delegation was explicit as mentioned or implicit such as when the Imam says 'I appoint you Judge of Judges', for he is the one who appoints and dismisses them. (Ayni, Fath) The judge is distinct from [the one appointed for] Jumu'ah, for it is permissible for him to appoint someone else even if the Imam did not permit him to appoint a deputy because it is on the verge of being missed since it is tied to a time whose performance lapses with its expiry. And judiciary (qada) is not like Jumu'ah because it is not time-bound. Then if the Imam dies before he begins the Jumu'ah, he may not appoint a deputy except one who attended the sermon because the sermon is a condition for it, so it cannot be valid without it. But if he has begun it, he may appoint a deputy who did not attend the sermon because the deputy begins anew, and the sermon is a condition for the commencement of Jumu'ah. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the judge's authority to appoint deputies. It explains that when the Imam explicitly or implicitly delegates the power to appoint or dismiss judges, the appointed judge has that authority, analogizing it to agency (wakalah). The judge for Jumu'ah prayer, however, can appoint a deputy even without the Imam's permission due to the time-sensitive nature of the prayer. The text also addresses nuances: if the Imam dies before starting Jumu'ah, only someone who attended the sermon can be appointed as deputy; but if the prayer has begun, a deputy who did not attend the sermon may be appointed. This distinction is based on the condition (sermon) for the validity of Jumu'ah. The Hanafi school holds this view based on istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the opportunity for Jumu'ah. The commentary relies on the explanations of 'Ayni and Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The act of appointing a deputy to perform judicial duties.
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation of authority by the Imam to the judge, explicitly or implicitly.
قاضي القضاة (qadi al-qudat): Chief judge appointed by the Imam with broad authority to appoint and dismiss subordinate judges.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a judge appointed for Jumu'ah prayer appoint a deputy who did not attend the sermon?
A) If the Imam has explicitly authorized it.
B) If the judge has begun the prayer.
C) If the judge has not yet begun the prayer.
D) Only if the deputy attended the sermon.

Key Takeaway
A judge may appoint a deputy only with the Imam's delegation, except for Jumu'ah where necessity permits it without delegation.

Qada — Judiciary

Conditions for Enforcing a Prior Judge's Ruling (Imda')
Rules on enforcement of prior judgments (imda')

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a subsequent judge must enforce a prior judge's ruling and identify the exceptions that allow overturning.

Core Idea
A second judge must enforce a prior judgment unless it clearly contradicts the Quran, famous Sunnah, or consensus.

This lesson explains when a judge who inherits a case from a predecessor must carry out the prior ruling. The Hanafi school emphasizes finality of judgments to prevent endless litigation, but allows overturning only if the original ruling violates definitive texts or consensus. We'll examine the precise conditions and exceptions as laid out in Kanz al-Daqaiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
The second judge enforces the first judge's ruling regardless of whether it agrees with his own opinion or whether the first judge remains, dies, or is dismissed. The text states this because the term 'judgment' is indefinite in a conditional context, making it general.
The general rule is derived from the wording: 'amḍāh' (he enforced it) and the principle that a judgment once passed is binding on later judges.
2
Recognize the Three Exceptions
The second judge may reject the first judgment if it contradicts: (1) the Quran (provided it is definitive in meaning), (2) the famous Sunnah (hadith known and accepted), or (3) consensus (ijma') of the early generations that is based on a sound legal proof.
Examples include judgments permitting a thrice-divorced woman to remarry without proper consummation (contradicting hadith) or permitting sale of an umm walad (contradicting consensus of the Successors).
3
Understand the Rationale of Ijtihad
The principle is that once a judgment is given on a matter subject to ijtihad, it is executed and not overturned by another ijtihad of equal or lower degree. The second judge's ijtihad does not outweigh the first because the first judgment has already been connected to the case.
This is based on the idea that both ijtihads are probable, and the first judgment, once executed, takes precedence.
4
Note the Special Condition: Knowledge of Scholarly Differences
The second judge must be aware of the existing scholarly differences in the jurisprudential matter. If he judges without such knowledge, his judgment is invalid according to the majority (of Hanafi scholars). This ensures that the second judge does not inadvertently contradict a valid ijtihad.
Referenced from Al-Jami' al-Saghir and the commentaries: 'شرطه: أن يكون عالماً باختلاف العلماء'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمضاه : [ أي أمضى القاضي المرفوع إليه حكم القاضي الآخر. (مع، فتح)] أي حكم بمقتضاه، وافق ذلك الحكم رأيه أو خالفه بقي الآخر على قضائه أو مات أو عزل؛ لأنه نكرة في سياق الشرط، فيعم، وقوله: "إن لم يخالف الكتاب" أي الحكم الذي لم يختلف في تأويله السلف كالقضاء بحل مزنية أبيه أو ابنه أو بصحة نكاح أم مزنية أو بنتها، ولابد من تقييد الكتاب بأن لا يكون قطعي الدلالة، وإلا فمخالفة المتواتر من كتاب أو سنة إذا كان قطعي الدلالة كفر ، وقوله والسنة المشهورة" كتحليل المطلقة الثلاث للزوج الأول بلا وطء الزوج الثاني؛ لأنه مخالف لحديث العسيلة، وكالقضاء بشاهد ويمين فإنه مخالف للحديث المشهور: "البينة على المدعي، واليمين على من أنكر"، وقيد بالمشهورة؛ احترازاً عن الحديث الغريب. وقوله: "والإجماع" أي الذي ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي، وغير المستند إليه يسمى خلافاً لا اختلافاً، والمعتبر: الاختلاف في الصدر الأول، ونظير مخالفة الإجماع: كما إذا قضى بجواز بيع أم الولد، فللقاضي الثاني أن ينقضه؛ لأنه مخالف لإجماع التابعين، والأصل في إمضاء القاضي ما رفع إليه إذا لم يكن مخالفاً للأدلة المذكورة: أن القضاء متى لاقى محلاً مجتهداً فيه ينفذ، ولا يرده غيره؛ لأن اجتهاد الثاني كاجتهاد الأول في أن كلاً منهما يحتمل الأول باتصال القضاء به، فلا ينتقض بما هو دونه درجة، وهو ما لم يتصل القضاء به، وفي "الجامع الصغير": وما اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى به القاضي، ثم جاء القاضي الآخر يرى غير ذلك، أمضاه، وقالوا: شرطه: أن يكون عالماً باختلاف العلماء، حتى لو قضى في فصل مجتهد فيه، وهو لا يعلم بذلك، لا يجوز قضاؤه عند عامتهم. (عيني، عناية، فتح) الخطأ، وقد رجح [؟] باب كتاب القاضي إن لم يخالف الكتاب والسنة المشهورة والإجماع، وينفذ القضاء بشهادة الزور في حكم القاضي الآخر العقود والفسوخ ظاهرا وباطنا، وهي أي بالشهادة الكاذبة الكتاب: مثل أن يقضي بحل متروك التسمية عامداً . (عيني) والإجماع: أي الذي ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي مثل القضاء بجواز نكاح الجدة. (معدن) وينفذ القضاء إلخ بأن ادعى رجل على امرأة نكاحا تجحد، وأقام الرجل عليها شاهدي زور ولا يعلم القاضي بكذب الشهود قضى بينهما بالنكاح وكذا في كل عقد وفسخ، وقوله: "ظاهرا" أي من حيث الظاهر فتسلم المرأة إلى الزوج، ويقول القاضي لها: سلمي نفسك إليه فإنه زوجك، وقوله: "وباطنا" أي ديانة بينه وبين الله فيحل الرجل وطؤها، ويحل لها التمكين، ويجب على الرجل النفقة والقسم، لكن للنفاذ باطنا شرطان: الأول: عدم علم القاضي بكذب الشهود، فلو علم به لم ينفذ قضاؤه، الثاني: كون المحل قابلا فإذا كانت المرأة تحت زوج أو معتدة أو مرتدة أو محرمة بمصاهرة أو برضاع، لم ينفذ، وهذا الحكم عند أبي حنيفة. وبه قالت الثلاثة وزفر، وله: قول علي له وهو ما روي أن رجلا ادعى بحضرة علي رضي الله عنه على امرأة نكاحاً وأقام الشاهدين، فقضي علي له بالنكاح، وقال للمرأة: "شاهداك زوجاك"؛ ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة بينهما من كل وجه، فلو لم ينفذ باطناً كان تمهيداً للمنازعة بينهما، وقد عهدنا بنفوذ مثل ذلك في الشرع، ألا ترى أن التفريق باللعان ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، وأحدهما كاذب بيقين. وصور المسائل كثيرة منها: إذا ادعى على امرأة رجل نكاحاً، وهي تجحد وأقام عليها شاهدي زور، وقضى القاضي بالنكاح بينهما حل للزوج وطؤها، وحل للمرأة التمكين منه عنده وعندهما: لا يحل له ذلك، ومنها: إذا قضى بالبيع بشهادة الزور، وهو على وجهين أحدهما أن يكون الدعوى من جانب المشتري بأن ادعى على غيره أنك بعت مني هذه الجارية، والآخر أن يكون من جانب البائع بأن قال: إنك اشتريت هذه الجارية مني، فإنه يحل للمشتري وطؤها في الوجهين، وكذلك صور الفسوخ كثيرة: منها: إذا ادعى أحد المتعاقدين فسخ العقد، وأقام بينة الزور، وفسخ القاضي يحل للبائع وطء الجارية ومنها: إذا ادعت على زوجها أنه طلقها ثلاثاً، وأقامت بينة زور، وقضى القاضي بالفرقة، وتزوجت بزوج آخر بعد انقضاء العدة، حل للزوج الوطء ظاهراً وباطناً . عنده لا عندهما. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢٦/٢] في العقود: كالنكاح والبيع والشراء ويشمل عقود التبرعات. (عيني، فتح ظاهراً: [ أي من حيث الظاهر بين الناس. (عيني)] أراد بالفسخ إبطال حكم العقد بأي وجه كان، فيعم الطلاق والإقالة والرد بالعيب. (عيني، فتح)
He enforced it: [meaning the judge to whom the judgment of another judge was referred enforced it. (Mughrib, Fath)] i.e., he ruled by its content, whether that judgment agreed with his opinion or differed, whether the other judge remained on his judgment or died or was dismissed; because it is an indefinite noun in the context of condition, so it is general. And his statement: 'As long as it does not contradict the Book' i.e., a judgment whose interpretation the predecessors did not differ upon, such as a judgment permitting marrying the daughter of one's father's or son's paramour, or the validity of marrying the mother of one's paramour or her daughter. And it is necessary to qualify the Book by it not being definitive in meaning, otherwise contradicting a mutawatir [text] from the Book or Sunnah that is definitive in meaning is disbelief. And his statement: 'and the famous Sunnah' such as permitting the thrice-divorced woman to her first husband without the second husband's intercourse, because it contradicts the hadith concerning the honey-drink (hadith al-'usaylah), and such as a judgment based on one witness and an oath, for it contradicts the famous hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.' And he qualified it by 'famous' to guard against rare hadith. And his statement: 'and consensus' i.e., that in which there is no disagreement based on a legal proof, and what is not based on such is called difference not valid disagreement, and consideration is given to disagreement in the early generations. An example of contradicting consensus: as if he judged the permissibility of selling an umm walad, then the second judge may overturn it because it contradicts the consensus of the Successors. The principle of enforcing a judge's decision that is referred to him, if it does not contradict the mentioned proofs, is that whenever a judgment encounters a matter subject to ijtihad, it is executed and not rejected by another, because the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, and since each of them is probable, the first is attached by the connection of the judgment to it, so it is not overturned by something of a lower degree, i.e., what is not connected to the judgment. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'What the jurists differed on, and a judge judged by it, then another judge came who held a different view, he enforces it.' And they said: the condition is that he be knowledgeable about the differences of the scholars, such that if he judged in a matter of ijtihad while not knowing that, his judgment is not valid according to the majority. (Ayni, Inayah, Fath) The error, and it has been preferred [؟] Chapter of the Judge's Book: As long as it does not contradict the Book, the famous Sunnah, and consensus, and the judgment is executed based on false testimony in the judgment of the other judge regarding contracts and rescissions externally and internally. That is, by false testimony. The Book: such as judging permissible to omit the basmalah intentionally. (Ayni) And consensus: which has no disagreement based on a legal proof, such as judging the permissibility of marrying a grandmother. (Ma'din) And the judgment is executed, etc., as when a man claims marriage to a woman who denies it, and he brings two false witnesses, and the judge does not know their falsehood, he judges marriage between them. Similarly in every contract and rescission. His statement 'externally' means from the apparent perspective, so the woman is handed over to the husband and the judge says to her: 'Surrender yourself to him for he is your husband.' His statement 'and internally' means religiously between him and Allah, so the man may have intercourse with her, and it is lawful for her to allow it, and the man must provide maintenance and division of nights. However, for internal execution there are two conditions: first, the judge's ignorance of the witnesses' falsehood; if he knows, his judgment is not executed. Second, the subject matter must be eligible: if the woman is under a husband, in waiting period, an apostate, or forbidden by marriage affinity or fosterage, it is not executed. This ruling is according to Abu Hanifa. And the three and Zufar also said this. His evidence is the statement of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) as narrated: a man claimed marriage before 'Ali against a woman, and brought two witnesses, and 'Ali judged marriage in his favor, and said to the woman: 'Your witnesses have married you.' Also because judgment is to put an end to dispute between them entirely; if it were not executed internally, it would pave the way for dispute. And we have seen such execution in the law: do you not see that separation by li'an is executed externally and internally, while one of them is certainly lying. Many scenarios exist: if a man claims marriage to a woman who denies it, and he brings false witnesses, and the judge rules marriage, then the husband may have intercourse with her, and the woman may allow him according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), that is not permissible. Another: if judgment is given for sale based on false testimony, which is of two types: one where the claim is by the buyer that you sold me this slave-girl, and the other where the seller says you bought this slave-girl from me; in both cases the buyer may have intercourse with her. Likewise many images of rescission: if one of the contracting parties claims rescission and brings false witnesses, and the judge rescinds, the seller may have intercourse with the slave-girl. Also: if a wife claims that her husband divorced her three times, and brings false witnesses, and the judge rules separation, and she marries another husband after the waiting period, the second husband may have intercourse externally and internally according to him, not according to both of them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 126/2] Concerning contracts: like marriage, sale, and purchase, and it includes gratuitous contracts. (Ayni, Fath) 'Externally' means from the apparent perspective among people. (Ayni) By 'rescission' he means abrogating the ruling of the contract in any manner, so it includes divorce, revocation, and return due to defect. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage covers two interconnected topics: (1) the conditions under which a subsequent judge must enforce a prior judge's decision (imda'), and (2) the ruling on judgments based on false testimony (shahadat al-zur). For the first topic, the text explains that a second judge must carry out the ruling of the first judge unless it contradicts the Quran, famous Sunnah, or consensus. Examples include judgments that violate clear texts (like allowing a thrice-divorced woman to remarry the first husband without proper consummation) or consensus (like selling an umm walad). The second judge may overturn only if the contradiction is clear and based on definitive proofs. Additionally, the second judge must be aware of scholarly differences to avoid invalid rulings. For the second topic, the text presents a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa (and the three, i.e., Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar), a judgment based on false testimony, when the judge is unaware of the falsehood and the subject is eligible, is effective both externally (the parties must act as if true) and internally (it is religiously permissible). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is effective only externally, not internally. Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the precedent of 'Ali (ra) who enforced a marriage with false witnesses, and the analogy with li'an where one party is certainly lying yet the separation is enforced. The text provides examples: marriage, sale, rescission, and divorce. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars and the practical need to end disputes.

Key Terms
إمضاء (imda'): Enforcement of a previous judge's ruling by a subsequent judge.
ظاهراً (zahiran): Externally, in the apparent legal sense; not used in this lesson.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule of imda', which of the following would allow a second judge to overturn a prior judgment?
A) The second judge has a stronger ijtihad on the matter.
B) The prior judgment contradicts a rare hadith (gharib).
C) The prior judgment contradicts the famous Sunnah.
D) The prior judgment was made by a judge who was later dismissed.

Key Takeaway
A subsequent judge must enforce a prior judgment unless it clearly contradicts the Quran, famous Sunnah, or consensus, and the second judge must be aware of scholarly differences.

Qada — Judiciary

Judgment on False Testimony: External and Internal Effect
Intra-Hanafi dispute on false testimony judgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the internal (batinan) effect of a judgment based on false testimony and state the conditions for its effectiveness according to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
According to Abu Hanifa, a judgment based on false testimony is effective both externally and internally; the two Sahibayn limit it to external effect only.

A judgment based on false testimony raises a unique legal question: is the ruling valid in the private conscience (batinan) or only in the public sphere (zahiran)? The Hanafi school split on this, with Abu Hanifa holding that it is effective both ways, and his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, restricting it to external effect. This lesson examines their proofs and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue and the Hanafi Positions
When a judge unwittingly bases a judgment on false testimony, is that judgment effective externally (the parties must act as if true) and also internally (religiously permissible for them)? Abu Hanifa says yes, the Sahibayn say only externally.
The positions are clearly stated in the text: 'وهذا الحكم عند أبي حنيفة' and 'عنده وعندهما: لا يحل له ذلك'.
2
Identify the Conditions for Internal Effect
Abu Hanifa conditioned internal enforcement on two things: (1) the judge's ignorance of the falsehood, and (2) the subject matter must be eligible (e.g., the woman is not already married or in iddah). If the judge knows, the judgment is not enforced internally.
These conditions are given explicitly: 'ولكن للنفاذ باطنا شرطان: الأول: عدم علم القاضي... الثاني: كون المحل قابلا'.
3
Analyze the Proofs of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa uses the precedent of 'Ali (ra) who enforced a marriage with false witnesses, saying 'Your witnesses have married you.' He also argues that judgment is to end dispute, and if it were not effective internally, it would perpetuate discord. He analogizes to li'an, where one spouse is certainly lying yet the separation is enforced both externally and internally.
The text presents the evidence: 'وله: قول علي... ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة... ألا ترى أن التفريق باللعان ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً'.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's Objection and the Response
The Sahibayn hold that false testimony is a sin and cannot render something religiously permissible in private. The Hanafi response is that the judge's ruling is based on his duty to decide on apparent evidence, and the public interest in finality overrides the private sinfulness of the witnesses.
While the text does not elaborate the Sahibayn's proof in full, their objection is implied by the contrasting rulings: 'عنده لا عندهما'.
5
Apply the Ruling Through Examples
The text provides several examples: marriage, sale, rescission, and divorce. For each, Abu Hanifa permits internal actions (e.g., intercourse) while the Sahibayn do not. This demonstrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
Examples include: 'إذا ادعى على امرأة... حل للزوج وطؤها... عنده وعندهما: لا يحل'.

(مع، فتح)] أي حكم بمقتضاه، وافق ذلك الحكم رأيه أو خالفه بقي الآخر على قضائه أو مات أو عزل؛ لأنه نكرة في سياق الشرط، فيعم، وقوله: "إن لم يخالف الكتاب" أي الحكم الذي لم يختلف في تأويله السلف كالقضاء بحل مزنية أبيه أو ابنه أو بصحة نكاح أم مزنية أو بنتها، ولابد من تقييد الكتاب بأن لا يكون قطعي الدلالة، وإلا فمخالفة المتواتر من كتاب أو سنة إذا كان قطعي الدلالة كفر ، وقوله والسنة المشهورة" كتحليل المطلقة الثلاث للزوج الأول بلا وطء الزوج الثاني؛ لأنه مخالف لحديث العسيلة، وكالقضاء بشاهد ويمين فإنه مخالف للحديث المشهور: "البينة على المدعي، واليمين على من أنكر"، وقيد بالمشهورة؛ احترازاً عن الحديث الغريب. وقوله: "والإجماع" أي الذي ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي، وغير المستند إليه يسمى خلافاً لا اختلافاً، والمعتبر: الاختلاف في الصدر الأول، ونظير مخالفة الإجماع: كما إذا قضى بجواز بيع أم الولد، فللقاضي الثاني أن ينقضه؛ لأنه مخالف لإجماع التابعين، والأصل في إمضاء القاضي ما رفع إليه إذا لم يكن مخالفاً للأدلة المذكورة: أن القضاء متى لاقى محلاً مجتهداً فيه ينفذ، ولا يرده غيره؛ لأن اجتهاد الثاني كاجتهاد الأول في أن كلاً منهما يحتمل الأول باتصال القضاء به، فلا ينتقض بما هو دونه درجة، وهو ما لم يتصل القضاء به، وفي "الجامع الصغير": وما اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى به القاضي، ثم جاء القاضي الآخر يرى غير ذلك، أمضاه، وقالوا: شرطه: أن يكون عالماً باختلاف العلماء، حتى لو قضى في فصل مجتهد فيه، وهو لا يعلم بذلك، لا يجوز قضاؤه عند عامتهم. (عيني، عناية، فتح) الخطأ، وقد رجح [؟] باب كتاب القاضي إن لم يخالف الكتاب والسنة المشهورة والإجماع، وينفذ القضاء بشهادة الزور في حكم القاضي الآخر العقود والفسوخ ظاهرا وباطنا، وهي أي بالشهادة الكاذبة الكتاب: مثل أن يقضي بحل متروك التسمية عامداً . (عيني) والإجماع: أي الذي ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي مثل القضاء بجواز نكاح الجدة. (معدن) وينفذ القضاء إلخ بأن ادعى رجل على امرأة نكاحا تجحد، وأقام الرجل عليها شاهدي زور ولا يعلم القاضي بكذب الشهود قضى بينهما بالنكاح وكذا في كل عقد وفسخ، وقوله: "ظاهرا" أي من حيث الظاهر فتسلم المرأة إلى الزوج، ويقول القاضي لها: سلمي نفسك إليه فإنه زوجك، وقوله: "وباطنا" أي ديانة بينه وبين الله فيحل الرجل وطؤها، ويحل لها التمكين، ويجب على الرجل النفقة والقسم، لكن للنفاذ باطنا شرطان: الأول: عدم علم القاضي بكذب الشهود، فلو علم به لم ينفذ قضاؤه، الثاني: كون المحل قابلا فإذا كانت المرأة تحت زوج أو معتدة أو مرتدة أو محرمة بمصاهرة أو برضاع، لم ينفذ، وهذا الحكم عند أبي حنيفة. وبه قالت الثلاثة وزفر، وله: قول علي له وهو ما روي أن رجلا ادعى بحضرة علي رضي الله عنه على امرأة نكاحاً وأقام الشاهدين، فقضي علي له بالنكاح، وقال للمرأة: "شاهداك زوجاك"؛ ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة بينهما من كل وجه، فلو لم ينفذ باطناً كان تمهيداً للمنازعة بينهما، وقد عهدنا بنفوذ مثل ذلك في الشرع، ألا ترى أن التفريق باللعان ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، وأحدهما كاذب بيقين. وصور المسائل كثيرة منها: إذا ادعى على امرأة رجل نكاحاً، وهي تجحد وأقام عليها شاهدي زور، وقضى القاضي بالنكاح بينهما حل للزوج وطؤها، وحل للمرأة التمكين منه عنده وعندهما: لا يحل له ذلك، ومنها: إذا قضى بالبيع بشهادة الزور، وهو على وجهين أحدهما أن يكون الدعوى من جانب المشتري بأن ادعى على غيره أنك بعت مني هذه الجارية، والآخر أن يكون من جانب البائع بأن قال: إنك اشتريت هذه الجارية مني، فإنه يحل للمشتري وطؤها في الوجهين، وكذلك صور الفسوخ كثيرة: منها: إذا ادعى أحد المتعاقدين فسخ العقد، وأقام بينة الزور، وفسخ القاضي يحل للبائع وطء الجارية ومنها: إذا ادعت على زوجها أنه طلقها ثلاثاً، وأقامت بينة زور، وقضى القاضي بالفرقة، وتزوجت بزوج آخر بعد انقضاء العدة، حل للزوج الوطء ظاهراً وباطناً . عنده لا عندهما. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢٦/٢] في العقود: كالنكاح والبيع والشراء ويشمل عقود التبرعات. (عيني، فتح ظاهراً: [ أي من حيث الظاهر بين الناس. (عيني)] أراد بالفسخ إبطال حكم العقد بأي وجه كان، فيعم الطلاق والإقالة والرد بالعيب. (عيني، فتح)
He enforced it: [meaning the judge to whom the judgment of another judge was referred enforced it. (Mughrib, Fath)] i.e., he ruled by its content, whether that judgment agreed with his opinion or differed, whether the other judge remained on his judgment or died or was dismissed; because it is an indefinite noun in the context of condition, so it is general. And his statement: 'As long as it does not contradict the Book' i.e., a judgment whose interpretation the predecessors did not differ upon, such as a judgment permitting marrying the daughter of one's father's or son's paramour, or the validity of marrying the mother of one's paramour or her daughter. And it is necessary to qualify the Book by it not being definitive in meaning, otherwise contradicting a mutawatir [text] from the Book or Sunnah that is definitive in meaning is disbelief. And his statement: 'and the famous Sunnah' such as permitting the thrice-divorced woman to her first husband without the second husband's intercourse, because it contradicts the hadith concerning the honey-drink (hadith al-'usaylah), and such as a judgment based on one witness and an oath, for it contradicts the famous hadith: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the one who denies.' And he qualified it by 'famous' to guard against rare hadith. And his statement: 'and consensus' i.e., that in which there is no disagreement based on a legal proof, and what is not based on such is called difference not valid disagreement, and consideration is given to disagreement in the early generations. An example of contradicting consensus: as if he judged the permissibility of selling an umm walad, then the second judge may overturn it because it contradicts the consensus of the Successors. The principle of enforcing a judge's decision that is referred to him, if it does not contradict the mentioned proofs, is that whenever a judgment encounters a matter subject to ijtihad, it is executed and not rejected by another, because the ijtihad of the second is like the ijtihad of the first, and since each of them is probable, the first is attached by the connection of the judgment to it, so it is not overturned by something of a lower degree, i.e., what is not connected to the judgment. And in Al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'What the jurists differed on, and a judge judged by it, then another judge came who held a different view, he enforces it.' And they said: the condition is that he be knowledgeable about the differences of the scholars, such that if he judged in a matter of ijtihad while not knowing that, his judgment is not valid according to the majority. (Ayni, Inayah, Fath) The error, and it has been preferred [؟] Chapter of the Judge's Book: As long as it does not contradict the Book, the famous Sunnah, and consensus, and the judgment is executed based on false testimony in the judgment of the other judge regarding contracts and rescissions externally and internally. That is, by false testimony. The Book: such as judging permissible to omit the basmalah intentionally. (Ayni) And consensus: which has no disagreement based on a legal proof, such as judging the permissibility of marrying a grandmother. (Ma'din) And the judgment is executed, etc., as when a man claims marriage to a woman who denies it, and he brings two false witnesses, and the judge does not know their falsehood, he judges marriage between them. Similarly in every contract and rescission. His statement 'externally' means from the apparent perspective, so the woman is handed over to the husband and the judge says to her: 'Surrender yourself to him for he is your husband.' His statement 'and internally' means religiously between him and Allah, so the man may have intercourse with her, and it is lawful for her to allow it, and the man must provide maintenance and division of nights. However, for internal execution there are two conditions: first, the judge's ignorance of the witnesses' falsehood; if he knows, his judgment is not executed. Second, the subject matter must be eligible: if the woman is under a husband, in waiting period, an apostate, or forbidden by marriage affinity or fosterage, it is not executed. This ruling is according to Abu Hanifa. And the three and Zufar also said this. His evidence is the statement of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) as narrated: a man claimed marriage before 'Ali against a woman, and brought two witnesses, and 'Ali judged marriage in his favor, and said to the woman: 'Your witnesses have married you.' Also because judgment is to put an end to dispute between them entirely; if it were not executed internally, it would pave the way for dispute. And we have seen such execution in the law: do you not see that separation by li'an is executed externally and internally, while one of them is certainly lying. Many scenarios exist: if a man claims marriage to a woman who denies it, and he brings false witnesses, and the judge rules marriage, then the husband may have intercourse with her, and the woman may allow him according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), that is not permissible. Another: if judgment is given for sale based on false testimony, which is of two types: one where the claim is by the buyer that you sold me this slave-girl, and the other where the seller says you bought this slave-girl from me; in both cases the buyer may have intercourse with her. Likewise many images of rescission: if one of the contracting parties claims rescission and brings false witnesses, and the judge rescinds, the seller may have intercourse with the slave-girl. Also: if a wife claims that her husband divorced her three times, and brings false witnesses, and the judge rules separation, and she marries another husband after the waiting period, the second husband may have intercourse externally and internally according to him, not according to both of them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 126/2] Concerning contracts: like marriage, sale, and purchase, and it includes gratuitous contracts. (Ayni, Fath) 'Externally' means from the apparent perspective among people. (Ayni) By 'rescission' he means abrogating the ruling of the contract in any manner, so it includes divorce, revocation, and return due to defect. (Ayni, Fath)

Commentary
This passage covers two interconnected topics: (1) the conditions under which a subsequent judge must enforce a prior judge's decision (imda'), and (2) the ruling on judgments based on false testimony (shahadat al-zur). For the first topic, the text explains that a second judge must carry out the ruling of the first judge unless it contradicts the Quran, famous Sunnah, or consensus. Examples include judgments that violate clear texts (like allowing a thrice-divorced woman to remarry the first husband without proper consummation) or consensus (like selling an umm walad). The second judge may overturn only if the contradiction is clear and based on definitive proofs. Additionally, the second judge must be aware of scholarly differences to avoid invalid rulings. For the second topic, the text presents a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa (and the three, i.e., Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar), a judgment based on false testimony, when the judge is unaware of the falsehood and the subject is eligible, is effective both externally (the parties must act as if true) and internally (it is religiously permissible). The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is effective only externally, not internally. Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the precedent of 'Ali (ra) who enforced a marriage with false witnesses, and the analogy with li'an where one party is certainly lying yet the separation is enforced. The text provides examples: marriage, sale, rescission, and divorce. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars and the practical need to end disputes.

Key Terms
شهادة الزور (shahadat al-zur): False testimony given knowingly in court.
ظاهراً (zahiran): Externally, in the apparent legal sense; the ruling is enforced publicly.
باطناً (batinan): Internally, between the person and God; the ruling is considered religiously valid.
لعن (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when one accuses the other of adultery.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is required for a judgment based on false testimony to be effective internally (batinan)?
A) The judge must be aware of the falsehood.
B) The subject matter must be eligible (e.g., woman not already married).
C) The witnesses must be from among the companions.
D) The judgment must be upheld by an appellate court.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the internal effect of judgments based on false testimony; Abu Hanifa's view that it is effective both externally and internally is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate

Effect of a Judge's Ruling Based on False Testimony: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Explains the effect of a judge's ruling based on false testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the inward and outward effect of a judgment based on false testimony, explain the conditions for inward effectiveness, and apply the ruling to practical cases.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling based on false testimony is effective both outwardly and inwardly according to Abu Hanifa, but only outwardly according to the Sahibayn.

When a judge issues a ruling based on false testimony, does that ruling have any effect in the sight of Allah (batinan), or is it only enforceable outwardly (zahiran)? This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents a critical intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The answer determines not only the permissibility of actions like marital intercourse but also the underlying philosophy of judicial authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the issue: whether a judgment based on false testimony is effective inwardly (batinan) or only outwardly (zahiran). Abu Hanifa holds it is effective both ways; the Sahibayn say it is only outward.
The inward effect means the ruling is considered valid religiously, e.g., intercourse becomes permissible for the husband.
2
Examine the conditions for inward effectiveness
List the two conditions from the text: (1) the judge must not know the witnesses are false; (2) the subject must be legally capable (e.g., woman not already married, not in iddah, etc.).
If the judge knows the truth, the ruling is not executed even outwardly? Actually, it may still be executed outwardly but not inwardly? The passage says 'if he knows, his judgment is not executed' – likely meaning not executed inwardly? It says 'لم ينفذ قضاؤه' which could mean the judgment is not effective at all? But the context is about inward effectiveness. Clarify in commentary.
3
Analyse the proofs (dalil)
Abu Hanifa's proof: the hadith of Ali (RA) where he judged a marriage based on witnesses and told the woman 'Your two witnesses have married you'. Also qiyas with li'an (mutual cursing) which is effective both ways despite one party lying. The Sahibayn's proof: false testimony is only an outward proof, like testimony of slaves or disbelievers which is not accepted inwardly.
Note the epistemological weight: both proofs are zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Apply to practical examples
Work through the examples given: marriage claim, sale, dissolution (divorce). For each, determine what is permissible inwardly according to each view.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the husband can have intercourse religiously.
5
Note the exception for absolute properties
The rule does not apply to claims of absolute ownership (al-amlak al-mursalah) without a specific cause. There, by consensus, the judgment is only outward. Similarly for inheritance. For gift and charity, there are two narrations.
This exception shows the principle that judgments cannot create legal relations that are impossible to establish.

إن لم يخالف الكتاب والسنة المشهورة والإجماع، وينفذ القضاء بشهادة الزور في
- ك د س م ز ف
حكم القاضي الآخر العقود والفسوخ ظاهرا وباطنا،

أي بالشهادة الكاذبة
الكتاب: مثل أن يقضي بحل متروك التسمية عامداً . (عيني) والإجماع: أي الذي ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي مثل القضاء بجواز نكاح الجدة. (معدن) وينفذ القضاء إلخ بأن ادعى رجل على امرأة نكاحا تجحد، وأقام الرجل عليها شاهدي زور ولا يعلم القاضي بكذب الشهود قضى بينهما بالنكاح وكذا في كل عقد وفسخ، وقوله: "ظاهرا" أي من حيث الظاهر فتسلم المرأة إلى الزوج، ويقول القاضي لها: سلمي نفسك إليه فإنه زوجك، وقوله: "وباطنا" أي ديانة بينه وبين الله فيحل الرجل وطؤها، ويحل لها التمكين، ويجب على الرجل النفقة والقسم، لكن للنفاذ باطنا شرطان: الأول: عدم علم القاضي بكذب الشهود، فلو علم به لم ينفذ قضاؤه، الثاني: كون المحل قابلا فإذا كانت المرأة تحت زوج أو معتدة أو مرتدة أو محرم رمة بمصاهرة أو برضاع، لم ينفذ، وهذا الحكم عند أبي حنيفة.
وبه قالت
والأصل فيه: أن كل شيء قضى به القاضي في الظاهر بتحريمه أو بإحلاله فهو في الباطن كذلك عنده، وعندهما: لا ينفذ إلا ظاهراً؛ لأن شهادة الزور حجة ظاهراً لا باطناً، فصار كما كان الشهود عبيدا، وكفاراً، الثلاثة وزفر، وله: قول علي له وهو ما روي أن رجلا إدعى بحضرة علي الله على امرأة نكاحاً وأقام الشاهدين، فقضي علي له بالنكاح، وقال للمرأة: "شاهداك زوجاك ؛ ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة بينهما من كل وجه، فلو لم ينفذ باطناً كان تمهيداً للمنازعة بينهما، وقد عهدنا بنفوذ مثل ذلك في الشرع، ألا ترى أن التفريق باللعان ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، وأحدهما كاذب بيقين.
وصور المسائل كثيرة منها: إذا ادعى على امرأة رجل نكاحاً، وهي تجحد وأقام عليها شاهدي زور، وقضى القاضي بالنكاح بينهما حل للزوج وطؤها، وحل للمرأة التمكين منه عنده وعندهما: لا يحل له ذلك، ومنها: إذا قضى بالبيع بشهادة الزور، وهو على وجهين أحدهما أن يكون الدعوى من جانب المشتري بأن ادعى على غيره أنك بعت مني هذه الجارية، والآخر أن يكون من جانب البائع بأن قال: إنك اشتريت هذه الجارية مني، فإنه يحل للمشتري وطؤها في الوجهين، وكذلك صور الفسوخ كثيرة: منها: إذا ادعى أحد المتعاقدين فسخ العقد، وأقام بينة ،الزور، وفسخ القاضي يحل للبائع وطء الجارية ومنها: إذا ادعت على زوجها أنه طلقها ثلاثاً، وأقامت بينة زور، وقضى القاضي بالفرقة، وتزوجت بزوج آخر بعد انقضاء العدة، حل للزوج الوطء ظاهراً وباطناً . عنده لا عندهما. [رمز الحقائق: ١٢٦/٢] في العقود: كالنكاح والبيع والشراء ويشمل عقود التبرعات. (عيني، فتح ظاهراً: [ أي من حيث الظاهر بين الناس. (عيني)] أراد بالفسخ إبطال حكم العقد بأي وجه كان، فيعم الطلاق والإقالة والرد بالعيب. (عيني، فتح)

لا في الأملاك المرسلة إلخ [ أي المطلقة التي لم يذكر سببها معينا. (عيني)] يعني لو قضى بشهادة زور في الأملاك المطلقة التي لا تثبت بدون أسبابها ينفذ قضاؤه ظاهراً لا باطنا؛ لأن في أسباب الملك تزاحماً، وليس تعيين البعض أولى من البعض، وإثبات الملك مطلقاً بغير سبب ليس في وسع البشر فتعين الإلغاء، بخلاف ما إذا ادعى سبباً معيناً كالبيع والشراء والإجارة والنكاح ونحوها فإنه ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، والحاصل: أن القضاء في الأملاك المرسلة بشهادة الزور لا ينفذ باطناً بالإجماع والإرث كالأملاك المطلقة، فلا ينفذ القضاء فيه بشهادة الزور باطناً وفي الهبة والصدقة روايتان عن أبي حنيفة. (عيني، فتح)
The chapter of the book of the judge. If it does not contradict the Book, the well-known Sunnah, and consensus, and the judgment is executed by false testimony in the judge's other rulings on contracts and dissolutions, outwardly and inwardly. It means by false testimony. The Book: like judging that something omitted intentionally is permissible. (Ayni) And consensus: that which has no dispute based on a legal proof, like judging the permissibility of marrying a grandmother. (Maden) And the judgment executes, etc., that a man claims marriage against a woman who denies, and the man brings two false witnesses and the judge does not know their falsehood, he judges the marriage between them, and likewise in every contract and dissolution. And his statement "outwardly" means from the outward perspective, so the woman is handed over to the husband, and the judge says to her: 'Submit yourself to him, for he is your husband.' And his statement "and inwardly" means religiously between him and Allah, so the man's intercourse with her becomes permissible, and it becomes permissible for her to allow it, and the man must provide maintenance and division of nights. But for effective execution inwardly, there are two conditions: first, that the judge does not know the falsehood of the witnesses; if he knows, his judgment is not executed. Second, that the subject matter is capable; if the woman is under a husband, or in waiting period, or an apostate, or forbidden by affinity or fosterage, it is not executed. And this ruling is according to Abu Hanifa. And with him they said. And the principle is: that everything the judge judges outwardly as prohibited or permissible is likewise inwardly according to him. But according to them (the two), it is only executed outwardly, because false testimony is a proof outwardly, not inwardly, so it becomes as if the witnesses were slaves or disbelievers, the three and Zufar. And his proof is the statement of Ali, which is what is narrated that a man claimed marriage in the presence of Ali against a woman and brought two witnesses, so Ali judged for him the marriage, and said to the woman: 'Your two witnesses have married you.' And because the judgment is to end the dispute between them completely, so if it were not executed inwardly, it would be a preparation for dispute between them. And we have seen the execution of such in the law; do you not see that separation by li'an (mutual cursing) is executed outwardly and inwardly, and one of them is certainly lying. And the forms of issues are many: among them, if a man claims marriage from a woman, and she denies, and he brings two false witnesses, and the judge judges the marriage between them, it becomes permissible for the husband to have intercourse with her, and permissible for the woman to allow him according to him; but according to them, it is not permissible for him. And among them, if he judges a sale by false testimony, and it is in two ways: one, that the claim is from the buyer, that he claims against another 'You sold me this slave-girl', and the other from the seller saying 'You bought this slave-girl from me', then it is permissible for the buyer to have intercourse with her in both ways. And likewise, the forms of dissolutions are many: among them, if one of the contracting parties claims dissolution of the contract and brings false evidence, and the judge dissolves, it becomes permissible for the seller to have intercourse with the slave-girl. And among them, if a wife claims against her husband that he divorced her three times, and she brings false evidence, and the judge rules separation, and she marries another husband after the waiting period, it becomes permissible for the husband to have intercourse outwardly and inwardly according to him, not according to them. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 126/2] Concerning contracts: like marriage, sale, and purchase, and it includes gratuitous contracts. (Ayni, Fath) Outwardly: [meaning from the outward perspective among people. (Ayni)] He meant by dissolution the annulment of the effect of the contract in any way, so it includes divorce, rescission, and return due to defect. (Ayni, Fath) Not in absolute properties, then he said: [meaning the unrestricted that does not mention its specific cause. (Ayni)] It means if he judges by false testimony in absolute properties that cannot be established without their causes, his judgment is executed outwardly, not inwardly, because the causes of ownership compete, and specifying one is not more preferable than another, and establishing absolute ownership without cause is not within human capacity, so nullification is inevitable. Contrary to if he claims a specific cause like sale, purchase, lease, marriage, and the like, then it is executed outwardly and inwardly. The conclusion: that the judgment in absolute properties by false testimony is not executed inwardly by consensus. And inheritance is like absolute properties, so the judgment therein by false testimony is not executed inwardly. And concerning gift and charity, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the legal effect of a judge's ruling that is based on false testimony (shahadat al-zur). The passage is of type intra-hanafi dispute, presenting the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding whether such a ruling is effective only outwardly (zahiran) or also inwardly (batinan). The commentator begins by stating that the judge's ruling is executed both outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions, provided it does not contradict the Qur'an, well-known Sunnah, or consensus. He then explains that outwardly means the woman is handed over to the husband, and inwardly means it is religiously permissible for him to have intercourse with her and for her to allow it, and he must provide maintenance. Two conditions are given for inward effectiveness: (1) the judge must not know the witnesses are false, and (2) the subject must be legally capable (e.g., the woman not already married or in waiting period). Abu Hanifa's position is that the ruling is effective both outwardly and inwardly, because the judgment's purpose is to end the dispute completely. The Sahibayn hold it is only effective outwardly, since false testimony is only a proof externally. The proof (dalil) for Abu Hanifa is the hadith where Ali (RA) judged a marriage based on witnesses and told the woman 'Your two witnesses have married you', implying the marriage was valid inwardly. Another proof is by analogy to the li'an ( mutual cursing) procedure, which is effective both outwardly and inwardly even though one party is certainly lying. The passage then provides multiple practical examples (thamanah al-khilaf): if a man claims marriage with false witnesses, Abu Hanifa says intercourse is permissible inwardly, but not according to the Sahibayn. The same applies to sales and dissolutions. An important qualification follows: the rule does not apply to 'absolute properties' (al-amlak al-mursalah) where no specific cause is claimed; there, the ruling is only effective outwardly by consensus, because establishing ownership without a specific cause is impossible. For gift and charity, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa. This passage thus clarifies the scope and limits of the inward effectiveness of a judgment based on false testimony within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شهادة الزور (shahadat al-zur): Testimony that is false, given intentionally by the witnesses.
ظاهراً وباطناً (zahiran wa batinan): Outwardly (in terms of legal appearance and enforcement) and inwardly (in terms of religious reality before Allah).
الأملاك المرسلة (al-amlak al-mursalah): Properties claimed without specifying a cause (e.g., simply claiming ownership without stating how it was acquired).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for a judgment based on false testimony to be effective inwardly (batinan) according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The witnesses must be Muslims.
B) The judge must not know the witnesses are false.
C) The subject must be a contract (not a dissolution).
D) The false testimony must be about absolute properties.

Key Takeaway
The inward effect of a judgment based on false testimony depends on the judge's ignorance of the falsehood and the subject's legal capacity, and is disputed between Abu Hanifa (effective both ways) and the Sahibayn (outward only).

Qada — Judiciary

Judgment on an Absent Person: Hanafi Rules and Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on the validity of judgment against an absent defendant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on judging an absent person, identify the exceptions (wakil, wasi, connected claims), and evaluate the opposing proof from the hadith of Hind.

Core Idea
An absent defendant cannot be judged without representation — hearing both sides is fundamental to valid judgment.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a core procedural question in Hanafi qada: when can a judge pass a ruling against a party who is not present? The Hanafi school takes a protective stance, requiring either a representative or a necessary connection to a present claim. We will examine the main rule, its proofs, the inter-madhhab dispute, and the exceptional cases that allow judgment in absentia.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general Hanafi rule
State the baseline: the judge should not judge against an absent person. The judgment is invalid (batil) unless an exception applies.
The rule applies to both judging for and against the absent.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith 'Do not judge one litigant without hearing the other' and how it requires both parties to be heard. The absence of the defendant prevents hearing, so no judgment.
The dalil is ahad, but its dalala is clear.
3
Contrast the opposing school's argument and Hanafi response
The three schools cite the hadith of Hind. Understand the Hanafi distinction that it was a fatwa, not a judgment.
The key is the nature of the Prophetic act.
4
Examine the first exception: representation
If a wakil (agent) or wasi (executor) appears on behalf of the absent, judgment is valid as if the absent were present. The musakhkhar (judge-appointed rep) is restricted.
The wakil is by the absent's own appointment; the wasi by law.
5
Examine the second exception: connected claims
If the claim against the absent is necessarily tied to a claim against a present person, judgment can bind the absent even without a representative.
Example: claiming a house in the hand of a present person bought from an absent seller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
