كالوكيل والوصى، أو يكون
اتفاقاً،
عطف على أن يحضره
مقام الغائب
(عيني، فتح) ولا يقضي: أي لا يصح قضاء القاضي على غائب ولا لغائب عندنا، وقالت الثلاثة: يجوز القضاء على الغائب بالبينة؛ لأنه عليها قضى لهند امرأة أبي سفيان بالنفقة وأبو سفيان غائب، فقال لها: "خذي من مال أبي سفيان ما يكفيك وولدك"، ولنا : قوله عليها لعلى الله: "لا تقض لأحد الخصمين حتى تسمع كلام الآخر، فإنك إذا سمعت كلام الآخر علمت كيف تقضي"، رواه أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي بمعناه، ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة، ولا منازعة هنا؛ لعدم الإنكار، فلا يصح. ولا حجة لهم في حديث هند؛ لأنه لم يكن قضاء، وإنما كان فتوى وإعانة لها على أخذ ماله، ألا ترى أنها لم تدع الزوجية و لم تقم البينة. (عيني، فتح) إلا أن يحضر أفاد الاستثناء أن القاضي إنما يحكم على الغائب والميت بحضرة وكيله وبحضرة وصيه، لا على الوكيل والوصي. وقوله: "كالوكيل" أفاد بالكاف عدم الحصر، فإن أحد الورثة ينتصب خصماً وكذا أحد عن الباقين شريكي الدين، وأحد الموقوف عليهم أي لو الوقف ثابتا. (فتح) كالوكيل أي كوكيل الغائب فإنه قائم مقامه بإنابته. (معدن) والوصي ويتقيد الوصي بإنابة الشرع احترازا عن المسخر من جهة القاضي وهو من ينصب القاضي. وكيلاً عن الغائب، ويسمع الخصومة عليه، ففيه اختلاف الروايتين، والمعنى: يجوز الحكم على الغائب إذا حضر من يقوم مقامه كالوكيل والوصي، ويجعل الغائب كأنه حاضر ، والحكم عليه، ولو أحضر رجل غيره عند القاضي ليسمع الخصومة عليه، والقاضي يعلم أنه مسخر وليس بخصم ، فالقاضي لا يسمع الخصومة عليه، والمذهب: أن القضاء على غائب بلا نائب لا يصح والمعتمد أن القضاء على المسخر لا يجوز إلا لضرورة. (عيني، فتح) أو يكون إلخ: أي يجوز الحكم على الغائب أيضاً فيما إذا كان الدعوى على الغائب سببا لازما للدعوى على الحاضر وهو نوعان: أحدهما: أن يكون على الحاضر والغائب شيئاً واحداً كمن ادعى داراً في يد غيره وأنكر الغير، أنها ملكه، وأقام المدعي البينة على ذي اليد أنه اشتراها من فلان الغائب تقبل بينته، ويثبت الحكم على الغائب والحاضر، حتى إذا حضر الغائب لزمه، ولا يحتاج إلى إعادة البينة، وكذا إذا ادعى في دار في يد غيره -
وادعى
And he does not judge against an absent person, unless someone who stands in his place appears, meaning the judge, like the agent (wakil) and the executor (wasi), or there is a connection, conjunction to 'that he appears' as a representative of the absent. (Ayni, Fath) 'And he does not judge' means that the judge's judgment against an absent person or for an absent person is not valid according to us. And the three said: It is permissible to judge against an absent person with evidence, because the Prophet (ﷺ) judged for Hind, the wife of Abu Sufyan, for maintenance while Abu Sufyan was absent, and said to her: 'Take from the wealth of Abu Sufyan what is sufficient for you and your child.' And our proof is his statement (ﷺ) to Ali (ﷺ): 'Do not judge for one of the two litigants until you hear the words of the other, for if you hear the words of the other, you will know how to judge.' Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi with similar meaning. And because judgment is to cut off dispute, and here there is no dispute due to lack of denial, so it is not valid. Their argument from the hadith of Hind is not conclusive, because it was not a judgment, but rather a fatwa and assistance for her to take his wealth. Do you not see that she did not claim marriage and did not provide evidence? (Ayni, Fath) 'Unless he appears' indicates the exception: the judge only judges against the absent and the deceased in the presence of his agent and his executor, not against the agent and executor. And his statement 'like the agent' indicates by the letter kaf the non-exclusivity, for one of the heirs may become a litigant, and likewise one of the remaining partners in debt, and one of the beneficiaries of a waqf if the waqf is established. (Fath) 'Like the agent' means like the agent of the absent, for he stands in his place by his deputization. (Maden) 'And the executor' is restricted to deputization by the law, as a precaution against the 'musakhkhar' (appointed representative) from the judge, who is one whom the judge appoints as an agent for the absent, and he hears the lawsuit against him. There is a difference in two narrations. The meaning: It is permissible to judge against the absent if someone who stands in his place appears, like the agent and executor, and the absent is considered as present, and judgment is passed against him. If a man brings someone else to the judge to hear the lawsuit against him, and the judge knows that he is a musakhkhar and not a litigant, then the judge does not hear the lawsuit against him. The madhhab is that judgment against an absent person without a representative is not valid, and the relied-upon opinion is that judgment against a musakhkhar is not permissible except for necessity. (Ayni, Fath) 'Or there is' etc.: meaning it is also permissible to judge against the absent when the claim against the absent is a necessary cause for the claim against the present, and it is of two types: one, that the present and the absent are one thing, like someone who claims a house in the hand of another, and the other denies it is his property, and the claimant provides evidence that the person in possession bought it from an absent person, his evidence is accepted, and the judgment is established against the absent and present, so that when the absent comes, it is binding on him, and he does not need to repeat the evidence. Likewise, if he claims a house in the hand of another, and he claims...
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the Hanafi position on judging an absent defendant (al-qada' 'ala al-gha'ib). The passage is of type inter-madhhab dispute, as the Hanafis oppose the majority (the three: Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) who permit judging an absent person based on evidence. The commentator begins by stating the core Hanafi rule: a judge should not judge against an absent person (or for him) unless a representative (like an agent or executor) appears. The proof (dalil) for the Hanafis is the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) instructing Ali (RA) not to judge one litigant without hearing the other. The purpose of judgment is to end a dispute, and without the absent party's denial, there is no dispute. The opposing view relies on the hadith where the Prophet allowed Hind to take maintenance from Abu Sufyan's wealth while he was absent. The Hanafi response is that this was not a judgment but a fatwa and assistance. The commentary then explains the exception: judgment on an absent is valid if a representative (wakil or wasi) appears. However, the judge cannot judge against the representative himself. The term 'wakil' is not exclusive; other representatives like one of the heirs or a partner in debt may also act. The musakhkhar (a person appointed by the judge to represent the absent) is treated differently: there is a difference of narration, but the relied-upon position is that judgment against a musakhkhar is not permissible except for necessity. Finally, another exception is when the claim against the absent is necessarily tied to a claim against a present person, e.g., if someone claims a house in the possession of a present person who bought it from an absent person, evidence can be accepted and the judgment will bind both. This shows the detailed conditions under which Hanafi law allows judgment on an absent person.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A person who is not present at the court session for a lawsuit against him.
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by the absent person to represent him in court.
مسخر (musakhkhar): A person appointed by the judge to represent the absent person, not by the absent's own appointment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a judge pass a valid judgment against an absent person?
A) Always, if the claimant provides evidence.
B) Never, under any circumstances.
C) Only if a representative (like an agent or executor) appears for the absent, or the claim is necessarily tied to a present party.
D) Only if the absent person is notified in advance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an absent defendant cannot be judged unless represented or the claim is linked to a present party — a rule rooted in the requirement to hear both sides.

Judgment with False Testimony in Absolute Property Claims: External vs Internal Validity
Explains that a judgment in absolute property claims with false testimony is valid only externally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a judgment based on false testimony in absolute property claims is valid externally but not internally, and identify the consensus (ijma) that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling on false testimony in absolute ownership claims gives worldly rights but is void before Allah.

When a judge issues a ruling based on false testimony, is the property truly owned by the claimant in the sight of Allah? The Hanafi school makes a critical distinction: in absolute property claims (where no specific cause of ownership is alleged), the judgment is effective only in worldly terms (zāhiran) but not in reality (bāṭinan). This is established by consensus (ijma) and rational necessity. Let's examine the reasoning and its scope, including the special cases of inheritance, gift, and charity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
The passage deals with a judge's decision based on false testimony (shahādat al-zūr) in absolute property claims (al-amlāk al-mursala). The ruling is that such a judgment is executed externally (nāfidh ẓāhiran) but not internally (lā nāfidh bāṭinan).
Absolute properties are those claimed without specifying a cause like sale or gift.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalīl)
The author cites consensus (ijmāʿ) as the evidence that the judgment is not valid internally. He also provides a rational proof: absolute ownership cannot be established without a cause; causes are numerous and none can be preferred over others; thus internal execution is impossible.
Consensus here is the collective agreement of scholars on this impossibility.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalālah
The consensus and rational reasoning converge: since it is beyond human capacity to establish ownership without a cause, the judgment must be nullified internally. The specific cause, if alleged, provides a basis for preference, making the judgment valid both externally and internally.
This distinguishes absolute claims from specific claims (e.g., sale, lease).
4
Note the Exceptions and Ikhtilāf
The passage states that inheritance (irth) is treated like absolute properties — judgment with false testimony is not valid internally. For gift (hiba) and charity (sadaqa), there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one equating them to absolute properties, another equating them to specific causes. The text does not resolve which is relied upon.
This intra-Hanafi difference shows the need for tarjīḥ based on other sources.
5
Evaluate the Tarjīḥ
The main ruling on absolute property claims is firmly established by ijma and rational proof; it is the muftā bihī position. The two narrations on gift/charity require further investigation beyond this passage.
The passage itself does not assign tarjīḥ for the ikhtilāf on gift/charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا في الأملاك المرسلة إلخ [ أي المطلقة التي لم يذكر سببها معينا. (عيني)] يعني لو قضى بشهادة زور في الأملاك المطلقة التي لا تثبت بدون أسبابها ينفذ قضاؤه ظاهراً لا باطنا؛ لأن في أسباب الملك تزاحماً، وليس تعيين البعض أولى من البعض، وإثبات الملك مطلقاً بغير سبب ليس في وسع البشر فتعين الإلغاء، بخلاف ما إذا ادعى سبباً معيناً كالبيع والشراء والإجارة والنكاح ونحوها فإنه ينفذ ظاهراً وباطناً، والحاصل: أن القضاء في الأملاك المرسلة بشهادة الزور لا ينفذ باطناً بالإجماع والإرث كالأملاك المطلقة، فلا ينفذ القضاء فيه بشهادة الزور باطناً وفي الهبة والصدقة روايتان عن أبي حنيفة.
Not in absolute properties… i.e., the unrestricted [properties] whose cause is not mentioned specifically. (Ayni) Meaning, if he judged with false testimony in absolute properties which cannot be established without their causes, his judgment is executed externally but not internally, because in the causes of ownership there is crowding, and specifying some is not better than others, and establishing ownership absolutely without a cause is not within human capacity, so nullification is determined. Unlike if he claimed a specific cause like sale, purchase, lease, marriage and the like, for then it is executed externally and internally. The conclusion: that judgment in absolute properties with false testimony is not executed internally by consensus, and inheritance is like absolute properties, so judgment therein with false testimony is not executed internally. And regarding gift and charity, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the book of Qada about the effect of a judgment based on false testimony. The key distinction is between absolute property claims (where no specific cause of ownership is alleged) and specific claims (where a cause like sale is mentioned). In absolute claims, the judge's ruling is effective only in worldly terms (zahiran) but not in reality (batiman) because there is no basis to prefer one cause over another, and establishing ownership without a cause is impossible. This is supported by ijma. Inheritance is treated the same. However, for gift (hiba) and charity (sadaqa), there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa, indicating some internal disagreement. The passage clarifies that when a specific cause is alleged, the judgment is valid both externally and internally.

Key Terms
الأملاك المرسلة (al-amlak al-mursala): Properties claimed without specifying a particular cause such as sale or gift; absolute ownership claims.
شهادة زور (shahadat al-zur): False testimony deliberately given to support a false claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a judgment with false testimony in absolute property claims not valid internally?
A) Because the judge did not intend justice.
B) Because establishing ownership without a cause is impossible and causes are numerous.
C) Because false testimony is always nullified.
D) Because the defendant was absent.

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling on false testimony in absolute property claims is effective only outwardly; it does not make the property lawful in reality, due to consensus on the impossibility of establishing ownership without a cause.

Judgment on an Absent Defendant and Its Exceptions
Inter-madhhab dispute on judgment in absentia with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on judgment against an absent defendant, explain the inter-madhhab dispute with proofs, and identify when judgment in absentia is permissible under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A judge cannot rule against an absent defendant; only a representative or a necessary link to a present claim makes it valid.

This lesson examines a fundamental procedural rule in Hanafi qada: the prohibition of judgment in absentia. We will explore the Hanafi proof from hadith, contrast it with the position of the three other imams, and then unpack the exceptions where judgment against an absent person is allowed. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between judicial rulings and non-judicial fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core Hanafi ruling on judgment against a gha'ib
State the general rule: the judge cannot legally issue a ruling (qada) against an absent person or in favor of an absent person. The ruling is batil (invalid).
The text uses 'لا يصح' meaning it is not valid.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil (proof)
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith 'Do not judge for one litigant until you hear the other' and the rational argument that judgment cuts off dispute, which requires denial from the absent party.
The hadith is transmitted by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi.
3
Understand the opposing school's proof
The three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) cite the hadith of Hind, where the Prophet allowed Hind to take maintenance from Abu Sufyan's wealth while he was absent.
This is their primary evidence for permitting judgment in absentia.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith of Hind
The Hanafi school distinguishes the incident as a fatwa and assistance, not a judicial ruling. Hind did not claim marriage or present evidence, so it was not a qada.
This is a critical distinction in Hanafi usul.
5
List the exceptions where judgment against an absent is permitted
Judgment is valid if: (1) a representative (wakil, wasi, heir, partner) appears for the absent; (2) the claim against the absent is a necessary cause (sabab) for the claim against a present party. If the claim is only a condition (shart) and the absent would be harmed, it is not permitted.
Type 1: one thing claimed against both. Type 2: two inseparable claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقضي: أي لا يصح قضاء القاضي على غائب ولا لغائب عندنا، وقالت الثلاثة: يجوز القضاء على الغائب بالبينة؛ لأنه عليها قضى لهند امرأة أبي سفيان بالنفقة وأبو سفيان غائب، فقال لها: "خذي من مال أبي سفيان ما يكفيك وولدك"، ولنا : قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "لا تقض لأحد الخصمين حتى تسمع كلام الآخر، فإنك إذا سمعت كلام الآخر علمت كيف تقضي"، رواه أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي بمعناه، ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة، ولا منازعة هنا؛ لعدم الإنكار، فلا يصح. ولا حجة لهم في حديث هند؛ لأنه لم يكن قضاء، وإنما كان فتوى وإعانة لها على أخذ ماله، ألا ترى أنها لم تدع الزوجية و لم تقم البينة. (عيني، فتح) إلا أن يحضر أفاد الاستثناء أن القاضي إنما يحكم على الغائب والميت بحضرة وكيله وبحضرة وصيه، لا على الوكيل والوصي. وقوله: "كالوكيل" أفاد بالكاف عدم الحصر، فإن أحد الورثة ينتصب خصماً وكذا أحد عن الباقين شريكي الدين، وأحد الموقوف عليهم أي لو الوقف ثابتا. (فتح) كالوكيل أي كوكيل الغائب فإنه قائم مقامه بإنابته. (معدن) والوصي ويتقيد الوصي بإنابة الشرع احترازا عن المسخر من جهة القاضي وهو من ينصب القاضي. وكيلاً عن الغائب، ويسمع الخصومة عليه، ففيه اختلاف الروايتين، والمعنى: يجوز الحكم على الغائب إذا حضر من يقوم مقامه كالوكيل والوصي، ويجعل الغائب كأنه حاضر ، والحكم عليه، ولو أحضر رجل غيره عند القاضي ليسمع الخصومة عليه، والقاضي يعلم أنه مسخر وليس بخصم ، فالقاضي لا يسمع الخصومة عليه، والمذهب: أن القضاء على غائب بلا نائب لا يصح والمعتمد أن القضاء على المسخر لا يجوز إلا لضرورة. (عيني، فتح) أو يكون إلخ: أي يجوز الحكم على الغائب أيضاً فيما إذا كان الدعوى على الغائب سببا لازما للدعوى على الحاضر وهو نوعان: أحدهما: أن يكون على الحاضر والغائب شيئاً واحداً كمن ادعى داراً في يد غيره وأنكر الغير، أنها ملكه، وأقام المدعي البينة على ذي اليد أنه اشتراها من فلان الغائب تقبل بينته، ويثبت الحكم على الغائب والحاضر، حتى إذا حضر الغائب لزمه، ولا يحتاج إلى إعادة البينة، وكذا إذا ادعى في دار في يد غيره - وادعى شفعة بأن ذا اليد اشتراها من فلان الغائب، وقال ذو اليد الدار داري لم اشترها من فلان الغائب، تقبل بينته ويثبت الحكم على الحاضر والغائب، وكذا إذا ادعى شخص دينا على أنه كفيل عن الغائب بأمره، فأقر الحاضر بالكفالة، وأنكر الدين، فأقام المدعي البينة أن له على الغائب ألف درهم تقبل بينته ويثبت الحكم على الحاضر والغائب. والنوع الثاني: أن يكون ما يدعيه عليهما شيئين، مثل أن يدعي القاذف أنه عبد فلان، فيجب عليه أربعون سوطا، فأقام المقذوف البينة أن مولاه الغائب قد أعتقه، فيجب عليه ثمانون سو وطاً، أو قال المشهود عليه: الشاهدان عبدان، فأقام المدعي البينة أن مولاهما أعتقهما، وهو يملكهما، فإن بينته تقبل، ويثبت العتق على الغائب؛ لأن الحقين كشيء واحد؛ إذ لا ينفك أحدهما عن الآخر؛ لأن ولاية الشهادة لا تنفك عن الحر، وحدّ الحر لا ينفك عن الأحرار. ثم إذا كان ما يدعيه على الغائب شرطاً لما يدعيه على الحاضر، ولا يكون سبباً ينظر، فإن كان الغائب يتضرر بالشرط لا تقبل بينته على الحاضر والغائب، مثل أن تقول المرأة لزوجها : إنك علقت طلاقي بطلاق فلان الغائب زوجته ثلاثاً، وأقامت بينة أن فلاناً طلق زوجته ثلاثاً، لم تقبل بينتها؛ لأنه يتضرر بذلك، وإن كان لا يتضرر، تقبل بأن قالت علقت طلاقي بدخول فلان الغائب الدار ، فأقامت بينة أنه دخل الدار، تقبل؛ لأنه لا ضرر عليه. رمز الحقائق: ۱۲۸/۲] (فتح) على الحاضر: فانتصب الحاضر خصما عنه فيجوز الحكم على الغائب أيضاً. (ط، عيني) فلان الغائب: تقبل بينته وثبت الحكم على الغائب والحاضر حتى إذا حضر الغائب وأنكر لا يلتفت إلى إنكاره. (ط، عيني)
And he does not judge: meaning that the judge's ruling against an absent person or for an absent person is not valid according to us. The three [imams] said: It is permissible to judge against the absent on the basis of evidence, because the Prophet ﷺ judged in favor of Hind, wife of Abu Sufyan, for maintenance while Abu Sufyan was absent, and he said to her: 'Take from the wealth of Abu Sufyan what suffices you and your children.' Our evidence is his saying ﷺ: 'Do not judge for one of the two litigants until you hear the speech of the other, for when you hear the speech of the other you will know how to judge.' Related by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi with similar meaning. And because judgment is for cutting off dispute, and there is no dispute here due to absence of denial, so it is not valid. And their argument from the hadith of Hind is not a proof because it was not a judgment, but rather a fatwa and assistance for her to take his wealth. Do you not see that she did not claim marriage and did not present evidence? (Ayni, Fath) Except that he attends: The exception indicates that the judge only rules against the absent and the deceased in the presence of his agent and in the presence of his executor, not against the agent and executor. His statement 'like the agent' indicates by the 'kaaf' that it is not exclusive, for one of the heirs may stand as a litigant, and similarly one of the partners in a debt, and one of the beneficiaries of a waqf if the waqf is established. (Fath) 'Like the agent' means like the agent of the absent, for he stands in his place by his appointment. (Ma'din) 'And the executor' is restricted to appointment by the law, as a precaution against the one appointed by the judge, i.e., someone the judge appoints as an agent for the absent and hears the lawsuit against him; there are two narrations concerning this. The meaning: It is permissible to judge against the absent if someone who stands in his place appears, like the agent and executor, and the absent is considered as present, and judgment is against him. If a man brings someone else to the judge to hear the lawsuit against him, while the judge knows that he is deputized and not a litigant, then the judge does not hear the lawsuit against him. The madhhab is that judgment against an absent without a representative is not valid. The relied-upon opinion is that judgment against a deputized person is not permissible except for necessity. (Ayni, Fath) 'Or be' etc.: meaning that judgment against the absent is also permissible when the claim against the absent is a necessary cause for the claim against the present. This is of two types: First: that what is claimed against the present and the absent is one thing, like someone claims a house in the possession of another, and that other denies that it is his property, and the plaintiff presents evidence that the possessor bought it from so-and-so who is absent; his evidence is accepted, and judgment is established against the absent and the present, so that when the absent appears it is binding on him, and there is no need to repeat the evidence. Similarly, if he claims a house in the possession of another and claims pre-emption on the basis that the possessor bought it from someone absent, and the possessor says the house is mine, I did not buy it from the absent; his evidence is accepted and judgment is established against the present and the absent. Similarly, if someone claims a debt on the basis that he is a guarantor for the absent by his order, and the present admits the guarantee but denies the debt, and the plaintiff presents evidence that he has a thousand dirhams against the absent; his evidence is accepted and judgment is established against the present and the absent. The second type: that what he claims against them are two things, like the slanderer claims he is the slave of so-and-so, so forty stripes are obligatory on him; then the slandered presents evidence that his absent master has emancipated him, so eighty stripes become obligatory. Or the one against whom testimony is given says: the two witnesses are slaves; the plaintiff presents evidence that their master has emancipated them and he owns them; his evidence is accepted, and emancipation is established against the absent, because the two rights are like one thing since they are inseparable, because the capacity for testimony is inseparable from freedom, and the punishment of a free person is inseparable from free persons. Then if what he claims against the absent is a condition for what he claims against the present, and is not a cause, then it is examined: if the absent would be harmed by the condition, his evidence is not accepted regarding the present and the absent, such as a woman saying to her husband: 'You have suspended my divorce on the divorce of so-and-so, his absent wife, three times,' and she presents evidence that so-and-so divorced his wife three times; her evidence is not accepted because he would be harmed by that. If he would not be harmed, it is accepted, as if she said: 'I suspended my divorce on the entry of so-and-so, the absent, into the house,' and she presents evidence that he entered the house; it is accepted because there is no harm to him. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 128/2) (Fath) 'Against the present': so the present stands as a litigant on his behalf, so it is permissible to judge the absent as well. (T, Ayni) 'So-and-so the absent': his evidence is accepted and judgment is established against the absent and the present, such that when the absent appears and denies, his denial is not heeded. (T, Ayni)
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage addresses a key procedural rule in Hanafi qada: the judge cannot issue a ruling against an absent party (gha'ib) or in favor of an absent party. The Hanafi position is contrasted with the three other schools (the 'thalatha' likely Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali) who permit it based on the Prophet's ﷺ instruction to Hind to take from Abu Sufyan's wealth. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, citing the hadith 'Do not judge until you hear both sides' which indicates the necessity of hearing both litigants; second, the rational argument that judgment is to settle a dispute, and there is no dispute without denial. The hadith of Hind is reinterpreted as a fatwa, not a judgment, since she did not claim marriage or present evidence. The passage then details exceptions: the judge can rule on the absent if a representative (agent, executor, or even an heir or partner) is present to stand in his place. Also, if the claim against the absent is a necessary cause for the claim against the present, judgment is permitted. Two types are given: when the claim is one thing (e.g., ownership of a house derived from a purchase from the absent) and when the claims are two but inseparable (e.g., emancipation of a witness affecting punishment). A further condition applies when the claim against the absent is merely a condition, not a cause: if the absent would be harmed, it is not permitted; otherwise, it is.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A person who is not present in the court and does not have a representative.
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by the absent party to represent him in court.
وصي (wasi): An executor appointed by the deceased or by the law to manage the affairs of the deceased or minors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an exception allowing judgment against an absent person according to the Hanafi school?
A) Presence of an agent (wakil)
B) Presence of an executor (wasi)
C) Presence of a court-appointed agent (musakhkhar)
D) Claim against the absent is a necessary cause for claim against the present

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits judgment against an absent defendant unless a representative stands in or the absent's claim is inseparable from a present claim.

Conditions for a Judge to Lend Orphan's Property
Ruling on judge lending orphan's property with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi judge may lend orphan's property and explain why lending is preferred over deposit.

Core Idea
A judge may lend orphan's property only when no executor exists, to a trustworthy borrower, for guaranteed preservation.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the permissibility and commendability (istihbab) of a judge lending the property of an orphan. It sets critical conditions—such as the absence of an executor and the borrower being trustworthy and wealthy—and contrasts lending with deposit, highlighting that a loan is guaranteed against loss. It also distinguishes the judge's authority from that of an executor, who is prohibited from lending and becomes liable if he does.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge lending (iqradh) the orphan's property. The ruling is 'mustahabb' (commendable) as stated by the term 'istihbaban' in the commentary.
The ruling is permissive and commendable, not obligatory.
2
List the conditions for the judge
Extract the conditions: (1) no executor exists for the orphan, (2) the borrower must be wealthy and trustworthy (mali' mu'taman), (3) the judge cannot find a mudaraba or a rental property purchase alternative, and (4) the judge writes a document (sakk) for the loan as a memorandum.
The condition 'no executor' is absolute; even if the executor was appointed by the judge, the executor is the one in charge.
3
Understand the rationale: lending vs. deposit
The text explains that a deposit (wadi'a) is not guaranteed against destruction, whereas a loan (qard) is guaranteed. The judge, due to many preoccupations, may prefer lending to ensure preservation with guarantee.
The guarantee shifts the risk of loss to the borrower, who must repay.
4
Note the restriction on the executor
The executor (wasi) is prohibited from lending the orphan's property. If he does, he is liable (damin) because the risk of destruction remains due to his inability to supervise properly (text incomplete).
This shows a key difference between the judge's authority (with guarantee and official capacity) and the executor's limited role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقرض القاضي مال اليتيم وهو من لا أب له. (ط، معدن] أي جاز للقاضي استحباباً أن يقرض مال اليتيم من مليء مؤتمن، حيث لا وصي له ولو منصوب القاضي؛ لأنه ممنوع من التصرف في ماله مع وجود وصيه في الصحيح، ولم يجد من يقبله مضاربة ولا مستغلاً يشتريه، وله أخذ المال من أب مسرف، ووضعه على يد عدل، وله إقراض اللقطة . من الملتقط، ومال الوقف والغائب، وله بيع منقوله إذا خاف التلف و لم يعلم مكانه. وقوله: "ويكتب الصك" أي لأجل تذكرة الإقراض؛ لأن في إقراض أموالهم مصلحتهم لبقائها محفوظة، فإن القاضي لكثرة أشغاله قد يعجز عن الحفظ بنفسه، ويحصل الحفظ بالوديعة ، أيضاً، لكنها لم تكن مضمونة بالهلاك، وبالقرض تصير محفوظة مضمونة، فيقرضها، وإن جحد المستقرض، فالقاضي يقدر على الاستخراج؛ لكونه معلوماً له، وبالكتابة يحصل الحفظ، وينتفي النسيان. وقوله : "لا" الوصي" أي ليس للوصي أن يقرض مال اليتيم، فإن فعل ضمن؛ لأن الحفظ والضمان وإن كانا موجودين بالإقراض، لكن مخافة الهلاك باقية؛ لعدم قدرة الوصي =
And the judge lends the property of the orphan – and he is one who has no father. (T, Ma'din) That is, it is commendable for the judge to lend the orphan's property to a wealthy trustworthy person, where there is no executor for him, even if appointed by the judge, because he is prevented from disposing of his property in the presence of his executor according to the correct position, and he does not find anyone to accept it as a mudaraba or a property to buy as a rental property. And he may take the money from a wasteful father and place it with a just person, and he may lend the lost property (luqata) to the finder, and the property of a waqf and of an absent person, and he may sell his movable property if he fears its destruction and does not know its location. And his statement: 'And he writes the document' means for the sake of a memorandum of the loan, because in lending their properties there is benefit for their preservation, for the judge due to his many preoccupations may be unable to preserve them himself, and preservation is also achieved by deposit, but that is not guaranteed against destruction, while by loan it becomes preserved and guaranteed. So he lends it, and if the borrower denies, the judge is able to extract it because it is known to him. And by writing, preservation is achieved and forgetfulness is removed. And his statement: 'No' to the executor' means that the executor may not lend the orphan's property, for if he does, he is liable, because preservation and guarantee, even though they exist through lending, the fear of destruction remains due to the executor's inability to... (text incomplete).
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage deals with the permissibility and commendability (istihbaban) of a judge lending the property of an orphan (yatim) who has no father. The judge may do so only if there is no executor (wasi) – whether the executor was appointed by the judge or by someone else – because the existence of an executor prevents the judge from directly administering the property. The judge must also find a trustworthy and wealthy borrower (mali' mu'taman). If a mudaraba or purchase of a rental property is possible, that might be preferred. The judge has other powers like taking money from a wasteful father, lending lost property, and waqf and absent persons' property. The judge is recommended to write a document (sakk) for the loan to preserve evidence. The reason for lending rather than keeping as a deposit (wadi'a) is that a deposit is not guaranteed, whereas a loan is guaranteed; also the judge may not be able to preserve the property himself. The final part states that the executor (wasi) is not allowed to lend the orphan's property; if he does, he becomes liable (damin) because the risk of loss remains high due to the executor's lack of authority? The text cuts off.

Key Terms
إقراض (iqradh): Lending money or property as a loan (qard) by the judge from the orphan's estate.
يتيم (yatim): A minor child who has lost his father.
صك (sakk): A document or certificate recording the loan, written for evidence.
وصي (wasi): Executor, guardian appointed to manage orphan's property.
وديعة (wadi'a): Deposit; property left for safekeeping without guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prefer the judge to lend orphan's property rather than keep it as a deposit?
A) Because lending yields more profit.
B) Because a loan is guaranteed against loss, while a deposit is not.
C) Because the judge cannot keep deposits.
D) Because orphans are not allowed to have deposits.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi judge may lend orphan's property only when there is no executor and the borrower is wealthy and trustworthy, and the loan is preferred over deposit because it guarantees the principal.

Evidence Involving Absent Persons: Cause vs Condition
Ruling on evidence when claim on present is based on absent's right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a cause (sabab) and a condition (shart) in claims involving absent persons, and apply the Hanafi rule that evidence is accepted only if the absent is not harmed by a condition.

Core Idea
If the present claim is based on the absent's right as a cause, evidence binds both; if it is a condition, it binds only if the absent suffers no harm.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq deals with a nuanced procedural rule: when a claimant brings evidence that involves an absent person's right in order to establish a claim against a present person, the judge must determine whether the absent's right is a cause (sabab) or a condition (shart) for the present claim. If it is a cause, the evidence binds both the present and the absent because the present person is considered a representative. If it is a condition, the judge must assess whether the absent would be harmed by the ruling; if harmed, the evidence is rejected, otherwise it is accepted. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a judge's proper handling of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of claims
First, determine whether what is claimed against the absent is the same thing as what is claimed against the present (type 1) or a different thing that is intertwined (type 2). In type 1, the absent's right is a cause (sabab) for the present claim. In type 2, it may be a condition (shart) or also a cause, but the text further distinguishes.
Examples: type 1 includes purchase from an absent seller or debt with a surety. Type 2 includes slander where the penalty depends on freedom status.
2
Apply the rule for type 1 (cause)
If the claim is the same thing (type 1), the present person is treated as a representative of the absent. The judge accepts evidence against the present, and the ruling binds both. The present person's denial does not bar the evidence.
The key principle: the present person is considered a representative by virtue of being involved in the same transaction.
3
Distinguish condition from cause in type 2
When the claims are two different things but linked (type 2), examine whether the absent's right is a condition (shart) for the present claim or a cause. If it is a cause, the same rule as type 1 may apply. If it is a condition, proceed to the harm test.
Example: in the slander case, the emancipation is not merely a condition but a cause that changes the penalty, so evidence is accepted without harm test.
4
Apply the harm test for conditions
If the absent's right is only a condition for the present claim, the judge must assess whether the absent would suffer legal harm (ḍarar) if the evidence is accepted. If harm exists, the evidence is rejected; if no harm, it is accepted.
Harm means legal detriment to the absent's rights, such as affecting his marital status or ownership. Mere inconvenience is not harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب كتاب القاضي
ما يدعى على الغائب سبباً لما يدعيه على الحاضر كمن ادعى عيناً في يد غيره أنه اشتراه من فلان الغائب ويقرض القاضي مال اليتيم العين أنه اشتراها من مثل دار المدعي أحد، فأقام المدعي بينة - شفعة بأن ذا اليد اشتراها من فلان الغائب، وقال ذو اليد الدار داري لم اشترها من فلان الغائب، تقبل بينته ويثبت الحكم على الحاضر والغائب، وكذا إذا ادعى شخص دينا على أنه كفيل عن الغائب بأمره، فأقر الحاضر بالكفالة، وأنكر الدين، فأقام المدعي البينة أن له على الغائب ألف درهم تقبل بينته ويثبت الحكم على الحاضر والغائب. والنوع الثاني: أن يكون ما يدعيه عليهما شيئين، مثل أن يدعي القاذف أنه عبد فلان، فيجب عليه أربعون سوطا، فأقام المقذوف البينة أن مولاه الغائب قد أعتقه، فيجب عليه ثمانون سو وطاً، أو قال المشهود عليه: الشاهدان عبدان، فأقام المدعي البينة أن مولاهما أعتقهما، وهو يملكهما، فإن بينته تقبل، ويثبت العتق على الغائب؛ لأن الحقين كشيء واحد؛ إذ لا ينفك أحدهما عن الآخر؛ لأن ولاية الشهادة لا تنفك عن الحر، وحدّ الحر لا ينفك عن ) الأحرار. ثم إذا كان ما يدعيه على الغائب شرطاً لما يدعيه على الحاضر، ولا يكون سبباً ينظر، فإن كان الغائب يتضرر بالشرط لا تقبل بينته على الحاضر والغائب، مثل أن تقول المرأة لزوجها : إنك علقت طلاقي بطلاق فلان الغائب زوجته ثلاثاً، وأقامت بينة أن فلاناً طلق زوجته ثلاثاً، لم تقبل بينتها؛ لأنه يتضرر بذلك، وإن كان لا يتضرر، تقبل بأن قالت علقت طلاقي بدخول فلان الغائب الدار ، فأقامت بينة أنه دخل الدار، تقبل؛ لأنه لا ضرر عليه. رمز الحقائق: ۱۲۸/۲] (فتح)
Chapter: Writing of the Judge. What is claimed against the absent as a cause for what is claimed against the present, such as someone claiming an object in the hand of another that he bought it from so-and-so absent. ... And the second type: that what he claims against them is two things, such as the slanderer claiming he is the slave of so-and-so, so forty lashes are due upon him, then the slandered person brings evidence that his absent master has emancipated him, so eighty lashes become due upon him. ... Then if what he claims against the absent is a condition for what he claims against the present, and is not a cause, then consideration is made: if the absent is harmed by the condition, his evidence is not accepted against the present and the absent, such as a woman saying to her husband: 'You have suspended my divorce upon the divorce of so-and-so absent, his wife three times,' and she brings evidence that so-and-so divorced his wife three times, her evidence is not accepted because he is harmed by that. But if he is not harmed, it is accepted, as when she says: 'I have suspended my divorce upon the entry of so-and-so absent into the house,' and she brings evidence that he entered the house, it is accepted because there is no harm upon him.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on the judge's writing in Hanafi fiqh. It addresses a specific scenario: when a claim against a present person is based on a right of an absent person. The text distinguishes two types. First, if the same thing is claimed on both—e.g., a person claims an object in the hand of another, alleging the present person bought it from an absent seller. The present person denies the purchase. If the claimant brings evidence that the present person bought it from the absent, the judge accepts it and the ruling binds both the present and the absent, because the present person is considered a representative for the absent in this matter. Similarly for debt with a surety. Second, if the claims are two different things but intertwined, like slander where the penalty depends on status—if the slanderer claims he is a slave (40 lashes), and the victim brings evidence that the absent master emancipated him (making him free, 80 lashes), the evidence is accepted because the two rights are inseparable: witness qualification and free-person penalty are tied. Then the text discusses conditions versus causes: if the absent person's right is merely a condition (not a cause) for the present claim, the judge must check if the absent would be harmed. If harmed, evidence is not accepted; if not harmed, it is accepted. Example: a wife saying her divorce is conditioned on the absent man divorcing his wife—if she brings evidence he did, it harms him, so not accepted. But if the condition is entry into a house (no harm), it is accepted.

Key Terms
غائب (ghā’ib): A person who is absent and against whom a claim is made; the judge may still rule based on evidence if the present person is a representative or if the absent is not harmed by a condition.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, presented to prove a claim.
سبب (sabab): A cause that directly gives rise to a legal effect; in this context, the absent's right is the cause for the present's liability, and evidence binds both.
شرط (shart): A condition whose occurrence triggers a legal effect; here, if the absent's action is a condition, the harm test applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which case is the evidence of a claimant accepted despite involving an absent person?
A) When the absent person is harmed by the condition.
B) When the absent person's right is a condition without legal harm.
C) When the present person denies being a representative.
D) When the claim involves two separate things unrelated to each other.

Key Takeaway
When a claim on a present person involves an absent person's right, the judge accepts evidence if the absent's right is a cause (binding both) or a harmless condition.

The Judge's Authority to Lend Orphan's Property and Restrictions on Executor and Father
Ruling on lending orphan property by judge, executor, and father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge may lend orphan's property, and distinguish the rulings for executor and father, applying the Hanafi principle of ability to recover.

Core Idea
Only the judge, who can enforce repayment, may lend orphan funds; executor and father cannot.

This passage from Kitab al-Qada addresses a critical fiduciary question: who may lend the property of an orphan to preserve it? The judge is granted a special permission, but this is not extended to the executor or father. Understanding the reasoning—rooted in the ability to recover the loan—is key to grasping the Hanafi position and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parties
The passage discusses the judge (qadi), the executor (wasi), and the father (ab).
Each has a different ruling regarding lending orphan's property.
2
Determine the ruling for each
The judge is permitted and recommended (istihbaban) to lend; the executor and father are prohibited.
The prohibition for executor and father is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
3
Understand the underlying rationale
The key factor is the ability to recover the loan if the borrower denies. The judge can enforce, but the executor and father generally cannot.
This is why lending by executor/father leads to personal liability (daman).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a weak narration allowing the father to lend, but the mufta bihi is prohibition due to risk of loss.
The text states: 'In one narration: it is permissible for him... and the apparent is that he lends to someone from whom he is safe from denial.'
5
Apply the principles to modern contexts
Consider how these rules apply to court-appointed guardians versus parents in today's financial landscape.
The judge's authority remains essential for protecting orphan wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقرض القاضي مال اليتيم وهو من لا أب له. (ط، معدن] أي جاز للقاضي استحباباً أن يقرض مال اليتيم من مليء مؤتمن، حيث لا وصي له ولو منصوب القاضي؛ لأنه ممنوع من التصرف في ماله مع وجود وصيه في الصحيح، ولم يجد من يقبله مضاربة ولا مستغلاً يشتريه، وله أخذ المال من أب مسرف، ووضعه على يد عدل، وله إقراض اللقطة . من الملتقط، ومال الوقف والغائب، وله بيع منقوله إذا خاف التلف و لم يعلم مكانه. وقوله: "ويكتب الصك" أي لأجل تذكرة الإقراض؛ لأن في إقراض أموالهم مصلحتهم لبقائها محفوظة، فإن القاضي لكثرة أشغاله قد يعجز عن الحفظ بنفسه، ويحصل الحفظ بالوديعة ، أيضاً، لكنها لم تكن مضمونة بالهلاك، وبالقرض تصير محفوظة مضمونة، فيقرضها، وإن جحد المستقرض، فالقاضي يقدر على الاستخراج؛ لكونه معلوماً له، وبالكتابة يحصل الحفظ، وينتفي النسيان. وقوله : "لا" الوصي" أي ليس للوصي أن يقرض مال اليتيم، فإن فعل ضمن؛ لأن الحفظ والضمان وإن كانا موجودين بالإقراض، لكن مخافة الهلاك باقية؛ لعدم قدرة الوصي = 

على الاستخراج؛ لأنه ليس كل قاض يعدل ولا كل بينة تقبل وقوله: "والأب" أي ولا يقرض الأب مال الصبي؛ لأنه لا يقدر على الاستخراج، فيضمن بالإقراض، وفي رواية: يجوز له ذلك؛ لأن ولاية الأب تعم المال والنفس كولاية القاضي وشفقته تمنعه من ترك النظر ،له والظاهر أنه يقرضه ممن يأمن جحوده، وإن أخذه الأب قرضاً لنفسه، فقيل له ذلك، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه ليس له ذلك. (عيني، عناية) ويكتب الصك بالقرض ندبا ليحفظ ؛ لأنه لكثرة أشغاله يخاف أن ينساه وهو كتاب الإقرار بالمال وغيره. (عيني،معدن) والأب أي ولا يقرض الأب مال ولده الصغير وكذا الملتقط مال الصغير، فإن أقرضوا ضمنوا لعجزهم عن التحصيل. (ط)
And the judge lends the orphan's property—and he is one who has no father. (T, Ma'din) i.e., it is permissible for the judge, as a recommendation, to lend the orphan's property to a trustworthy wealthy person, when there is no executor for him, even if appointed by the judge; because he is prevented from disposing of his property in the presence of his executor in the correct view, and he does not find anyone to accept it as a mudaraba nor a property to buy. And he may take the property from an extravagant father and place it with a just person. And he may lend the found object (luqata) from the finder, and the property of the endowment (waqf) and the absent. And he may sell his movable property if he fears its loss and does not know his location. And his statement: 'And he writes the document' i.e., as a memorandum of the loan; because in lending their properties is their interest for their preservation. Indeed, the judge due to his many occupations may become incapable of preserving it himself, and preservation is also achieved by deposit, but it is not guaranteed against destruction, and by loan it becomes preserved and guaranteed, so he lends it. And if the borrower denies, the judge is able to extract it because it is known to him. And by writing, preservation is achieved and forgetfulness is eliminated. And his statement: 'Not the executor' i.e., it is not for the executor to lend the orphan's property; if he does, he is liable, because preservation and guarantee, even if they exist by lending, but the fear of destruction remains due to the executor's inability to extract... because not every judge is just nor every evidence accepted. And his statement: 'And the father' i.e., the father does not lend the property of the minor child, because he cannot extract it, so he becomes liable by lending. And in one narration: it is permissible for him because the father's guardianship encompasses property and person like the judge's guardianship, and his compassion prevents him from neglecting his interest. And it appears that he lends to someone from whom he is safe from denial. And if the father takes a loan for himself, it has been said he may do so, and Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he may not. (Ayni, Inaya) And he writes the document for the loan as a recommendation to preserve it, because due to his many occupations he fears forgetting it. And it is a document of acknowledgment for property and otherwise. (Ayni, Ma'din) And the father: i.e., the father does not lend the property of his young child, and similarly the finder of the minor's property; if they lend, they are liable due to their inability to recover. (T)
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Qada (Book of Judiciary) discusses the rules regarding the lending of an orphan's property by the judge, the executor (wasi), and the father. The judge is permitted, and in fact recommended (istihbaban), to lend the orphan's money to a reliable and wealthy person, provided there is no executor. This is because the judge has the authority and ability to recover the loan if the borrower denies it, as he is known and the judge can use his authority. The purpose is preservation and guarantee—unlike a deposit (wadi'a) which is not guaranteed. The judge also writes a document (sakk) as a memorandum to avoid forgetfulness. However, the executor (wasi) is prohibited from lending because he generally cannot recover the loan if denied, though some say he can. The father (ab) is also prohibited, though there is a narration allowing it due to his comprehensive guardianship. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the father cannot lend, and if he does, he is liable (damin). The text also notes that the judge may lend the property of an absent person, waqf, and luqata (found object) under certain conditions. This showcases the Hanafi school's concern for the preservation of the orphan's wealth and the limitation of authority to those who can enforce repayment.

Key Terms
يتيم (yatīm): A minor child who has lost his father; his property is under the guardianship of the judge or executor.
وصي (waṣī): An executor appointed by the deceased father or by the judge to manage the orphan's affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the executor (wasi) is prohibited from lending the orphan's property?
A) He lacks the compassion of the father.
B) He is unable to recover the loan if the borrower denies.
C) The judge must do all financial transactions.
D) Lending is not a form of preservation.

Key Takeaway
Only the judge, who has enforcement authority, may lend orphan's property; an executor or father may not, and becomes liable if they do.

The Father Lending Minor's Property: Prohibition and Liability
Ruling on father lending minor's property with conditions and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father lending his minor child's property and explain why the father becomes personally liable.

Core Idea
A father cannot lend his minor's property; if he does, he personally guarantees the debt.

This passage clarifies a critical limitation on the father's guardianship. While the father has broad authority over his minor child's property, the power to lend is withheld because he lacks the qadi's enforcement power (istikhraj). The consequence is personal liability (daman). We will explore the ruling, its reasoning, and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses the father lending the minor's property. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is not permitted (makruh tahrimi).
The father is distinguished from the qadi, who can write the loan document.
2
Understand the reasoning based on istikhraj
The key legal reason: the father cannot enforce collection of the debt (istikhraj), unlike the qadi who has judicial authority. Thus, if he lends, he becomes liable for any loss.
This is a classic example of linking permissibility to the ability to execute the contract's consequences.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration (riwaya) that allows it based on the father's comprehensive guardianship and compassion. However, the zahir riwayah is prohibition, and that is the mufta bihi position.
The ikhtilaf hinges on whether istikhraj is a necessary condition for lending.
4
Apply the ruling to the father borrowing for himself
If the father takes the minor's money as a loan for himself, it is disputed. Some say permissible; Hasan narrates from Abu Hanifa that it is not allowed.
This shows the principle of conflict of interest.
5
Consider the recommendation to write the document
Although the father should not lend, the qadi is recommended to write the loan document (sakk) for preservation, as a general rule for any loan.
Writing the document is mandub, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكتب الصك، لا الوصي والأب. أي القاضي على الاستخراج؛ لأنه ليس كل قاض يعدل ولا كل بينة تقبل وقوله: "والأب" أي ولا يقرض الأب مال الصبي؛ لأنه لا يقدر على الاستخراج، فيضمن بالإقراض، وفي رواية: يجوز له ذلك؛ لأن ولاية الأب تعم المال والنفس كولاية القاضي وشفقته تمنعه من ترك النظر، له والظاهر أنه يقرضه ممن يأمن جحوده، وإن أخذه الأب قرضاً لنفسه، فقيل له ذلك، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه ليس له ذلك. (عيني، عناية) ويكتب الصك بالقرض ندبا ليحفظ؛ لأنه لكثرة أشغاله يخاف أن ينساه وهو كتاب الإقرار بالمال وغيره. (عيني،معدن) والأب أي ولا يقرض الأب مال ولده الصغير وكذا الملتقط مال الصغير، فإن أقرضوا ضمنوا لعجزهم عن التحصيل. (ط)
And he writes the document, not the guardian and the father. Meaning: the qadi, for extraction; because not every judge is just nor every evidence accepted. And his saying: "and the father" means: and the father should not lend the property of the minor; because he is unable to extract (the debt), so he guarantees (is liable) by lending. And in a narration: it is permissible for him; because the guardianship of the father encompasses property and person like the guardianship of the qadi, and his compassion prevents him from abandoning consideration for him. And apparently he lends to someone from whom he is safe from denial. And if the father takes it as a loan for himself, then it is said that is permissible for him. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not have that (right). He writes the document for the loan as recommended to preserve it; because due to the abundance of his occupations, he fears forgetting it. And it is a document of acknowledgement of property and other than it. And the father: meaning, the father should not lend the property of his minor child. Likewise the finder of lost property (should not lend) the property of the minor. If they lend, they guarantee (are liable) due to their inability to collect.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a commentary clarifying the ruling on the father (or guardian) writing a loan document and lending the minor's property. The text states that the qadi writes the document, not the guardian (wasi) or the father. However, it explains that the father is prohibited from lending the minor's money because he cannot effectively collect the debt—unlike the qadi who has authority to enforce collection. If the father lends, he becomes personally liable (yadman). There is an alternate narration (riwaya) allowing it based on the father's comprehensive guardianship and compassion, but the relied-upon view is that it is not permitted. The father may lend if he is confident the borrower is trustworthy. If the father borrows for himself, it is disputed: some allow it, but Hasan ibn Ziyad reports from Abu Hanifa that it is not allowed. Writing the loan document is recommended (mandub) for preservation due to the qadi's many preoccupations. The same ruling applies to the finder of lost property (multaqit): if they lend the minor's found property, they are liable.

Key Terms
صك (sakk): A written document recording a loan or acknowledgement of debt, used as evidence.
استخراج (istikhraj): The process of extracting or collecting a debt through legal authority.
ضمن (damana): To become liable or guarantee; if the father lends without authority, he must compensate for any loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a father lends his minor child's money to someone and the borrower denies the debt?
A) The father is not liable because he is the guardian.
B) The father is liable because he cannot enforce collection.
C) The qadi is responsible for collection.
D) The minor must repay the father.

Key Takeaway
The father's guardianship does not extend to lending the minor's property because he lacks enforcement power; liability follows unauthorized lending.

The Hanafi Law of Arbitration: Definition, Conditions, and Scope
Introduction to arbitration Hanafi definition, proofs, conditions, and scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and conditions of valid arbitration (tahkim) in the Hanafi school and identify which disputes are excluded from its authority.

Core Idea
Arbitration is like a compromise – it cannot overrule fixed punishments or blood-rights beyond the parties' control.

Arbitration (tahkim) is a branch of judiciary where parties agree to appoint a qualified person to settle their dispute. While similar to a qadi's ruling, the arbitrator's authority is limited to the consenting parties and cannot extend to matters like hudud or retaliation. This lesson examines its proofs, conditions, and boundaries according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Define tahkim and identify its legal status
Understand that tahkim is a branch of qada (judiciary). The arbitrator (muhakkam) has authority only over those who consent, unlike a qadi whose authority is general.
The phrase 'min furu al-qada' indicates it is subordinate to the judiciary.
2
List the proofs establishing tahkim
Identify the three sources: Quran (4:35), Sunnah (Sa'd ibn Mu'adh arbitration), and Ijma (companion consensus).
The Quranic verse is specific to marital disputes but extended by analogy to all disputes.
3
Identify conditions for the appointing party (muhakkim) and the arbitrator (muhakkam)
The muhakkim must be sane and adult; freedom and Islam are not required. The muhakkam must meet all qualifications of a qadi: sane, adult, free, Muslim, not convicted of slander, and known (not unknown).
Women and sinners are considered fit for judgeship according to the text, so they may serve as arbitrators.
4
Recognize subject-matter limitations
Tahkim is not valid in hudud, qisas, and diya on the aqila (clan) because these involve rights beyond the parties' control. Exception: if the killer confesses, diya can be enforced on him.
The limitation is based on the nature of tahkim as a form of sulh (compromise); the parties cannot permit what they do not own.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas and hadd qadhf
Some Hanafi scholars (Abu Bakr al-Razi, Shams al-A'imma) permit tahkim in qisas and hadd qadhf because they are private rights of the victim or guardian. The relied-upon position prohibits it.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; both views have strong evidence.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التحكيم أي في بيان أحكامه حكما رجلاً ليحكم بينهما، فحكم ببينة أو إقرار أو نكول في غير حدّ وقود ودية أي الاثنان أي جعلاه حكما ذلك الرجل رجل محكم" على العاقلة، صح لو صلح المحكم قاضيا، أي حكمه من المدعى عليه أي قصاص مع قبول باب التحكيم هو مصدر من حكم بتشديد الكاف إذا جعله حكما بفتحتين. (عيني)] هو من فروع القضاء، وتأخيره من حيث أن الحكم أدنى مرتبة من القاضي؛ لاقتصار حكمه على من رضي بحكمه، وعموم ولاية القاضي، وهو مشروع بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة. أما الكتاب، فقوله تعالى: ﴿فَابْعَثُوا حَكَمَا مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَحَكَماً مِنْ أَهْلِهَا (النساء: ٣٥) نزلت في تحكيم الزوجين، وأما السنة فروي أنه علي نزل على حكم سعد بن معاذ الله في بني قريظة لما اتفقت اليهود على الرضاء بحكمه، وعليه إجماع الصحابة وركنه: اللفظ الدال عليه الآخر، وشرطه من جهة المحكم بالكسر : العقل والبلوغ لا الحرية والإسلام، فيصح تحكيم ذمّي ذمياً، ومن جهة المحكم بالفتح: صلاحيته للقضاء. (فتح، عناية) رجلاً: أي معلوما؛ إذ لو حكما أول من يدخل المسجد لم يجز إجماعاً للجهالة، والعطف بالفاء في قوله: "فحكم" اتفاقي لا قيد، وأفاد بقوله: "لو صلح قاضياً" جواز تحكيم المرأة والفاسق؛ لصلاحيتهما للقضاء، ولأن الحكم بمنزلة القاضي فيما بينهما، فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في القاضي، حتى لو حكما كافراً أو عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف أو صبياً، لا يجوز إن كان المتخاصمان مسلمين، وإن حكم أهل الذمة ذميا جاز؛ لأنه من أهل الشهادة فيما بينهم، وكذا يجوز تقليده القضاء؛ ليحكم بين أهل الذمة. غير وإنما قال: "في غير حد وقود ودية على العاقلة؛ لأن تحكيمهما بمنزلة الصلح بينهما، وليس لهما ولاية على دمهما، ولهذا لا يملكان إباحته وكذا لا ولاية لهما على العاقلة ولا ينفذ حكم من حكماه على العاقلة، ولا على القاتل؛ لعدم التزام العاقلة حكمه؛ لكونه مخالفا لحكم الشرع؛ لأن الدية تجب على العاقلة لا على القاتل، ولو ثبت القتل بإقرار القاتل نفذ حكمه عليه أيضاً؛ لأن العاقلة لا تعقل ما ثبت بالإقرار، وقال أبو بكر الرازي في القصاص: أن ينبغي يجوز التحكيم في القصاص؛ لأن ولي المقتول لو استوفى القصاص من . يرفع إلى السلطان جاز، فكذلك إذا حكم فيه من حقوق بني آدم وقال شمس الأئمة في "شرح أدب القاضي": من أصحابنا من بجواز التحكيم في القصاص وحد القذف؛ لأن الاستيفاء إليهما. رمز الحقائق: ١٢٩/٢] (فتح) بينهما: أي بين الاثنين المتخاصمين نكول أي امتناع المدعى عليه عن اليمين. (معدن) المحكم: بتشديد الكاف وفتحها أي صلح أن يكون قاضيا. (عيني قاضيا يعني يكون مكلفا حرا مسلما غير محدود في قذف؛ لأنه بمنزلة القاضي فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في القاضي. (عيني، ط)
Chapter of arbitration: concerning the explanation of its rulings. Two men appointed a man to judge between them, and he judged with evidence or confession or refusal (to take oath) in other than fixed punishments, retaliation, and blood-money upon the clan. (Meaning: the two litigants appointed that man as an arbitrator). "A man who is fit (to be a judge)" (i.e., his judgment is valid) if the arbitrator is fit to be a judge. (Meaning: his judgment against the defendant, i.e., retaliation, with acceptance). The chapter of arbitration is derived from the verb 'hakkama' (with shaddah on kaaf) meaning to make him an arbitrator (with two fatha). It is one of the branches of judiciary, and its being placed after (the chapter of the judge) is because the arbitrator is of a lower rank than the qadi, since his jurisdiction is limited to those who consent to his judgment, whereas the qadi's authority is general. It is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus of the Ummah. As for the Book, Allah says: 'And if you fear a breach between the two, appoint an arbitrator from his family and an arbitrator from her family' (4:35) revealed concerning arbitration between spouses. As for the Sunnah, it is narrated that 'Ali submitted to the judgment of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh regarding Banu Qurayzah when the Jews agreed to accept his judgment. And upon it is the consensus of the companions. Its pillar (rukn) is the utterance indicating it (the appointment). Its condition on the part of the one appointing (muhakkim, with kasr): sanity and puberty, not freedom and Islam; so it is valid for a dhimmi to appoint a dhimmi. And on the part of the arbitrator (muhakkam, with fatha): his fitness for judgeship. "A man" means known; for if they appoint the first person to enter the mosque, it is not valid by consensus due to ignorance. The conjunction with 'fa' in 'fa-hakama' is incidental, not a condition. And his saying 'if he is fit to be a judge' indicates the permissibility of appointing a woman or a sinful person, because they are fit for judgeship. Because the arbitrator is like a judge between them, so what is required for a judge is required for him. Hence if they appoint a disbeliever, a slave, one who has been flogged for slander, or a minor, it is not valid if the litigants are Muslims. But if the people of the dhimmah appoint a dhimmi, it is valid, because he is among those qualified for testimony among themselves. Similarly, it is permissible to appoint him as a judge to judge among the people of the dhimmah. And he only said: "in other than fixed punishments, retaliation, and blood-money upon the clan" because their arbitration is like a compromise between them, and they have no authority over their blood; therefore they cannot permit it. Likewise, they have no authority over the clan, and the judgment of the one they appointed does not take effect on the clan nor on the killer, because the clan is not bound by his judgment, it being contrary to the ruling of Shari'ah, because blood-money is obligatory on the clan, not on the killer. However, if the killing is established by the killer's confession, his judgment takes effect on him as well, because the clan does not bear liability for what is established by confession. Abu Bakr al-Razi said concerning retaliation: it is appropriate that arbitration in retaliation be allowed, because if the guardian of the slain executes retaliation without raising the matter to the sultan, it is permissible; likewise if he arbitrates therein, it being from among the rights of human beings. And Shams al-A'imma said in Sharh Adab al-Qadi: among our companions are those who permit arbitration in retaliation and the hadd of slander, because the right of execution belongs to them. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 2/129) (Fath) "between them" means between the two litigants. "Refusal" means the defendant's refusal to take the oath. (Ma'din) "al-Muhakkam" (with shaddah on kaaf and fatha on it) means one who is fit to be a judge. (Ayni) "A judge" means he must be legally responsible, free, Muslim, not having been flogged for slander; because he is like a judge, so conditions for a judge are required for him. (Ayni, T)
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on arbitration (tahkim) in a Hanafi fiqh work. It defines tahkim as a branch of judiciary, with its own rules. The page states that tahkim is legislated by Quran (verse on family arbitration), Sunnah (Sa'd ibn Mu'adh's arbitration), and consensus. The pillar (rukn) is the utterance of appointment. The one appointing (muhakkim) must be sane and adult, but need not be free or Muslim; thus a dhimmi can appoint a dhimmi arbitrator. The arbitrator (muhakkam) must be qualified to be a judge: sane, adult, free, Muslim, not a convicted slanderer. If the litigants are Muslims, they cannot appoint a disbeliever, slave, flogged slanderer, or minor. However, if dhimmis appoint a dhimmi, it is valid. The arbitrator's authority is limited: he cannot adjudicate in fixed punishments (hudud), retaliation (qisas), or blood-money (diya) on the clan (aqila), because these involve rights of Allah or third parties beyond the litigants' authority. However, if the killer confesses, the arbitrator can enforce diya on him directly. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether arbitration is valid in qisas and hadd of qadhf; some scholars like Abu Bakr al-Razi and Shams al-A'imma allow it, reasoning that these are private rights of the litigants.

Key Terms
تحكيم (tahkim): The act of appointing an arbitrator to settle a dispute between two parties; the arbitrator's authority is limited to those who consent.
محكم (muhakkam): The arbitrator himself; he must be qualified to be a judge.
محكم (muhakkim): The person who appoints the arbitrator; only sanity and puberty are required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid arbitration according to the Hanafi school?
A) Two Muslims appoint a dhimmi.
B) Two dhimmis appoint a dhimmi.
C) Two Muslims appoint a woman with judgeship qualifications.
D) Two Muslims appoint a minor.

Key Takeaway
Arbitration (tahkim) is a valid but limited form of dispute resolution in Hanafi law; it cannot overrule fixed punishments or blood-rights unless the parties have authority.

Qada — Judiciary
beginner

Arbitration (Tahkīm): Definition, Conditions, and Excluded Cases
Defines arbitration, conditions for arbitrator, and excludes hadd, qisas, diyah on 'aqila

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tahkīm, identify the conditions for its validity, and explain why it is excluded in hadd, qisas, and diyah on the ʿāqila according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Arbitration is valid only by consent and excludes cases where individual authority over blood is absent.

Arbitration (tahkīm) is a voluntary dispute resolution mechanism where both parties agree to appoint a private judge. This lesson examines its definition, the conditions required for the arbitrator, and the specific cases where Hanafi law prohibits arbitration. Understanding these limits is crucial for distinguishing arbitration from the general judiciary (qaḍāʾ).

Guided Path
1
Define tahkīm and its legal basis
Identify the definition from the text: appointing a man to judge between two parties. Then note the proofs: Quran (4:35), Sunnah (Sa'd ibn Mu'adh incident), and consensus. This establishes the permissibility of tahkīm.
Tahkīm is a form of dispute resolution that relies on mutual consent.
2
Identify the conditions for the arbitrator
Distinguish between conditions for the one appointing (muḥakkim) and the one appointed (muḥakkam). The muḥakkim must be sane and adult; the muḥakkam must be suitable for judgeship (sane, adult, free, Muslim, not flogged for slander). A known arbitrator is required to avoid ignorance.
A dhimmi can arbitrate among dhimmis.
3
List the excluded cases and rationale
Arbitration is invalid in hadd punishments, qisas (retaliation), and diyah on the ʿāqila (collective blood money). The reason is that arbitration is like a settlement (ṣulḥ), and parties have no authority over blood or fixed penalties. The ʿāqila is not bound without consent.
The parties cannot permit forbidden acts.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (Abu Bakr al-Razi, Shams al-A'imma) permit arbitration in qisas and hadd for qadhf, analogizing to the guardian's right to execute qisas without a judge. Understand their reasoning and note that the majority position is more precautionary.
This ikhtilaf shows the scope of ijtihad within the school.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Test a case: two Muslims agree to arbitrate a theft accusation. The arbitrator must be a qualified judge, and the case must not be a hadd penalty. If it is a financial dispute, arbitration is valid. If hadd applies, the ruling is invalid.
Always check the nature of the dispute first.

باب التحكيم أي في بيان أحكامه حكما رجلاً ليحكم بينهما، فحكم ببينة أو إقرار أو نكول في غير حدّ وقود ودية على العاقلة، صح لو صلح المحكم قاضيا، أي الاثنان أي جعلاه حكما ذلك الرجل رجل محكم على العاقلة، أي حكمه من المدعى عليه أي قصاص مع قبول باب التحكيم هو مصدر من حكم بتشديد الكاف إذا جعله حكما بفتحتين. (عيني) هو من فروع القضاء، وتأخيره من حيث أن الحكم أدنى مرتبة من القاضي؛ لاقتصار حكمه على من رضي بحكمه، وعموم ولاية القاضي، وهو مشروع بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة. أما الكتاب، فقوله تعالى: ﴿فَابْعَثُوا حَكَمَا مِنْ أَهْلِهِ وَحَكَماً مِنْ أَهْلِهَا (النساء: ٣٥) نزلت في تحكيم الزوجين، وأما السنة فروي أنه علي نزل على حكم سعد بن معاذ الله في بني قريظة لما اتفقت اليهود على الرضاء بحكمه، وعليه إجماع الصحابة وركنه: اللفظ الدال عليه الآخر، وشرطه من جهة المحكم بالكسر : العقل والبلوغ لا الحرية والإسلام، فيصح تحكيم ذمّي ذمياً، ومن جهة المحكم بالفتح: صلاحيته للقضاء. (فتح، عناية) رجلاً: أي معلوما؛ إذ لو حكما أول من يدخل المسجد لم يجز إجماعاً للجهالة، والعطف بالفاء في قوله: "فحكم" اتفاقي لا قيد، وأفاد بقوله: "لو صلح قاضياً" جواز تحكيم المرأة والفاسق؛ لصلاحيتهما للقضاء، ولأن الحكم بمنزلة القاضي فيما بينهما، فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في القاضي، حتى لو حكما كافراً أو عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف أو صبياً، لا يجوز إن كان المتخاصمان مسلمين، وإن حكم أهل الذمة ذميا جاز؛ لأنه من أهل الشهادة فيما بينهم، وكذا يجوز تقليده القضاء؛ ليحكم بين أهل الذمة. غير وإنما قال: "في غير حد وقود ودية على العاقلة" ; لأن تحكيمهما بمنزلة الصلح بينهما، وليس لهما ولاية على دمهما، ولهذا لا يملكان إباحته وكذا لا ولاية لهما على العاقلة ولا ينفذ حكم من حكماه على العاقلة، ولا على القاتل؛ لعدم التزام العاقلة حكمه ; لكونه مخالفا لحكم الشرع; لأن الدية تجب على العاقلة لا على القاتل، ولو ثبت القتل بإقرار القاتل نفذ حكمه عليه أيضاً; لأن العاقلة لا تعقل ما ثبت بالإقرار، وقال أبو بكر الرازي في القصاص: أن ينبغي يجوز التحكيم في القصاص; لأن ولي المقتول لو استوفى القصاص من . يرفع إلى السلطان جاز، فكذلك إذا حكم فيه من حقوق بني آدم وقال شمس الأئمة في "شرح أدب القاضي": من أصحابنا من بجواز التحكيم في القصاص وحد القذف; لأن الاستيفاء إليهما. رمز الحقائق: ١٢٩/٢] (فتح) بينهما: أي بين الاثنين المتخاصمين نكول أي امتناع المدعى عليه عن اليمين. (معدن) المحكم: بتشديد الكاف وفتحها أي صلح أن يكون قاضيا. (عيني قاضيا يعني يكون مكلفا حرا مسلما غير محدود في قذف; لأنه بمنزلة القاضي فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في القاضي. (عيني، ط) قال
Chapter of Arbitration: Explanation of its rulings. They appoint a man to judge between them, so he judges by evidence, confession, or refusal to take oath in other than hadd, qisas, and diyah on the 'aqila. It is valid if the arbitrator is suitable to be a judge. Arbitration is a branch of judiciary. Its delay in being mentioned is because a hakam (arbitrator) is of a lower rank than a judge, since his judgment is limited to those who consent to his judgment, whereas a judge's authority is general. It is legislated by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus. The Book: 'Send an arbitrator from his family and an arbitrator from her family' (4:35). The Sunnah: 'Ali submitted to the judgment of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh regarding Banu Qurayza when the Jews agreed to his judgment. There is consensus of the Companions. Its pillar: the expression indicating it. Its condition regarding the arbitrator (with kasr): sanity and adulthood, not freedom and Islam, so it is valid to appoint a dhimmi for a dhimmi. Regarding the one appointed (with fatha): his suitability for judgeship. 'A man' means known; if they appoint the first person to enter the mosque, it is not valid by consensus due to ignorance. The conjunction 'fa' in 'so he judges' is incidental, not a condition. His statement 'if the arbitrator is suitable to be a judge' indicates the validity of appointing a woman or a corrupt person, because they are suitable for judgeship, because the arbitrator is like a judge between them, so the conditions of a judge are required. Thus if they appoint a disbeliever, a slave, one who has been flogged for slander, or a child, it is not valid if the litigants are Muslims. If the people of dhimmah appoint a dhimmi, it is valid, because he is among their eligible witnesses. Similarly, it is valid to appoint him as a judge to judge between dhimmis. So he said 'in other than hadd, qisas, and diyah on the 'aqila' because their arbitration is like a settlement between them, and they have no authority over their blood, so they do not possess the right to permit it. Also, they have no authority over the 'aqila, and the judgment of the one they appointed does not bind the 'aqila, nor the killer, because the 'aqila did not accept his judgment, and it contradicts the legal ruling because diyah is due on the 'aqila not the killer. If the killing is proven by the killer's confession, his judgment binds him because the 'aqila does not bear what is proven by confession. Abu Bakr al-Razi said regarding qisas: arbitration should be permissible in qisas because if the guardian of the slain were to execute qisas without going to the sultan, it would be valid; similarly if arbitration is made in it, it is from the rights of humans. Shams al-A'imma said in Sharh Adab al-Qadi: Some of our scholars permit arbitration in qisas and in hadd for slander because the execution is in their hands. (Fath) 'between them' means between the two litigants. 'Nukul' means the defendant's refusal to take oath. (Ma'din) 'al-muhakkam' (with tashdid on kaf and fatha) means he is suitable to be a judge: i.e., he must be legally responsible, free, Muslim, not flogged for slander, because he is like a judge and the conditions of a judge are required in him. (Ayni, T) He said.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on arbitration (tahkim) in Kitab al-Qada. It first defines tahkim as appointing a man (muhakkam) to judge between two parties. The ruling states that if the arbitrator gives a judgment based on evidence (bayyinah), confession (iqrar), or refusal to take oath (nukul), it is valid, provided the arbitrator is qualified to be a judge (salih li'l-qada). The passage then clarifies the legal basis: Qur'an (4:35), Sunnah (the case of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh), and consensus. The conditions for the arbitrator are similar to those of a judge: sanity and adulthood are required from the side of the one who appoints (muhakkim bihi), while from the side of the appointed (muhakkam bihi) suitability for judgeship is required, which includes Islam, freedom, and not having been flogged for slander. However, among dhimmis, a dhimmi arbitrator is valid. The passage then addresses the scope of arbitration: it is valid in all cases except hadd punishments, qisas (retaliation), and diyah (blood money) on the 'aqila (the clan's collective liability). The reason is that arbitration is akin to a settlement, and the parties have no authority over their own blood. Moreover, the 'aqila is not bound by the arbitration because they did not consent. There is a notable ikhtilaf: some scholars like Abu Bakr al-Razi and Shams al-A'imma permit arbitration in qisas and hadd for qadhf because the right of execution belongs to the individual. The passage concludes with further clarifications on the terms 'muhakkam' and 'nukul'.

Key Terms
تحكيم (tahkīm): Appointing a person to judge between two parties by mutual consent.
المحكم (al-muḥakkim (with kasr) and al-muḥakkam (with fatha)): The one who appoints (muḥakkim) and the one appointed (muḥakkam).
صلح (ṣulḥ): Settlement; arbitration is likened to a settlement because it requires mutual agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases is arbitration (tahkim) not valid according to the majority Hanafi view?
A) A dispute over a debt
B) A case of theft (hadd)
C) A dispute over the price of a house
D) A disagreement about the return of a deposit

Key Takeaway
Arbitration (tahkīm) is valid only by mutual consent and is excluded in hadd, qisas, and diyah on the ʿāqila because parties lack authority over these divinely prescribed or collective matters.
