وإن قال قاض عزل لرجل: أخذت منك ألفاً ودفعتها إلى زيد قضيت به عليك، أي ألف درهم بألف حق له عليك اللام متعلق يقال، فقال الرجل: أخذته ظلما فالقول للقاضي، وكذا لو قال: قضيت بقطع يدك في حق إنه فعله وهو قاض أي بطريق الظلم أي يصدق القاضي بلا يمين إذا كان المقطوع يده والمأخوذ منه المال مقراً أنه فعله وهو قاض في المسألة الأولى في المسألة الثانية. القاضي - ثم القضاة أربعة : عالم عادل، وعالم جائر، وجاهل عادل وجاهل جائر، فيقبل قول الأول محملاً ومفسراً، وإن كان عادلاً جاهلاً يستفسر، فإن أحسن تفسيره وجب تصديقه، وإلا لا، وإن كان جاهلاً فاسقاً أو عالماً فاسقاً لا يقبل قوله إلا أن يعاين سبب الحكم، وهو الشهود، أو يشهد بذلك مع القاضي عدل في حق يثبت بشاهدين، ومعناه: أن يشهد القاضي والعدل على شهادة الذين شهدوا بسبب الحد، وقال محمد آخراً: لا يقبل قول القاضي حتى يعاين الحجة، وكثير من مشايخنا أخذوا برواية محمد في هذا؛ لفساد أكثر قضاة هذا الزمان لاسيما في قضاة البلاد الذين يتولون برشوة وهم في أنفسهم جهلاء، وأكثرهم فسقة وهذا يقتضي أن لا يقبل كتابه أيضاً إلا أنهم تركوا هذا القول في الكتاب للحاجة إليه، وجه ظاهر الرواية: أن القاضي أخبر عما يملك إنشائه، ومن تمكن من الإنشاء عما أخبر به لم يتهم في خبره، ولأن في تصديقه طاعة، فيجب تصديقه. (عيني، فتح، عناية) عزل : أي عن القضاء وهو صفة قاض. (معدن قضيت أي حال كونه قد قضيت. فالقول للقاضي: [أي بغير عين؛ لأنه ثبت أنه فعل ذلك في حال قضائه. (عيني)] لأن المقضي عليه لما أقر أنه فعله في قضائه كان الظاهر شاهداً للقاضي؛ إذ القاضي لا يقضي بالجور ظاهراً، ولا يمين على القاضي؛ لأنه لو لزمه يمين صار خصماً، وقضاء الخصم لا ينفذ، والحاصل أن القول للقاضي، ولا يلزمه الضمان إذا كان المأخوذ ماله والمقطوع يده مقراً بأنه فعل ذلك وهو قاض بالاتفاق، فعلم من هذا أن المقطوع يده والمأخوذ ماله إذا زعم أنه لم يكن قاضياً يومئذ، وإنما فعل ذلك قبل التقليد أو بعد العزل، كان القول قول المدعي، نص عليه شمس الأئمة السرخسي. وقال صاحب "الهداية": القول للقاضي أيضاً في الصحيح؛ لأنه أسند فعله إلى حالة معهودة منافية للضمان، فصار كما إذا قال الرجل: طلقت أو أعتقت وأنا مجنون والجنون كان معلوماً بين الناس، فالقول قوله، حتى لا يقع الطلاق والعتاق؛ لإضافته إلى حالة منافية للإيقاع، ولو أقر القاطع والآخذ في هذا الفصل بما أقر به القاضي يضمنان؛ لأنهما أقرا بسبب الضمان، وقول القاضي مقبول في دفع الضمان نفسه، لا في إبطال عن عن غيره، بخلاف سبب الضمان الأول بأنه ثبت فعله في قضائه بالتصادق (عيني، فتح، عناية) حق: وقال المقضي عليه: فعلته ظلماً. And if a dismissed judge says to a man: 'I took a thousand dirhams from you and gave it to Zaid, and I ruled it against you' – meaning a thousand dirhams as a right due to him from you, the lam is attached to 'said' – and the man says: 'You took it unjustly,' then the statement (al-qawl) is the judge's. Similarly, if he said: 'I ruled the cutting of your hand in a right' – meaning he did it unjustly – meaning the judge is believed without oath if the one whose hand is cut and from whom money is taken admits that he did it while he was a judge. In the first issue (the money) and the second issue (the hand). The judge – then the judges are four: a knowledgeable just one, a knowledgeable unjust one, an ignorant just one, and an ignorant unjust one. So the statement of the first (knowledgeable just) is accepted whether he explains in detail or in summary. And if he is just but ignorant, he is asked for explanation: if he explains well, he must be believed; otherwise not. And if he is ignorant and immoral or knowledgeable and immoral, his statement is not accepted unless the reason for the ruling is witnessed, which is the witnesses, or he testifies with the judge (when the judge is) just in a right that is proven by two witnesses. Its meaning is that the judge and the just person testify to the testimony of those who witnessed the cause of the hadd. And Muhammad said later: The judge's statement is not accepted until he witnesses the evidence. Many of our mashayikh adopted Muhammad's narration due to the corruption of most judges of this time, especially the judges of the regions who take bribes and are ignorant in themselves, and most of them are immoral. This necessitates that his letter should also not be accepted except that they abandoned this opinion in the book due to necessity. The rationale of the apparent riwayah is that the judge reports what he has the power to initiate, and one who has the power to initiate concerning what he reports is not accused in his report, and because believing him is obedience, so he must be believed. (Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah) 'Dismissed' means removed from the judiciary, and it is a description of the judge. (Ma'dan) 'I ruled' meaning in the state that he had already ruled. The statement is the judge's: [meaning without specification because it is established that he did that during his judgeship. (Ayni)] Because when the one against whom the ruling was made admits that he did it during his judgeship, the apparent is a witness for the judge, since the judge does not rule unjustly apparently, and there is no oath upon the judge because if an oath were required, he would become a litigant, and the judgment of a litigant is not executed. The conclusion is that the statement is the judge's, and he is not liable for guarantee if the one whose money was taken and whose hand was cut admits that he did it while he was a judge by agreement. So it is understood from this that if the one whose hand was cut and from whom money was taken claims that he was not a judge that day, but did it before appointment or after dismissal, the statement is that of the claimant (the one who says it was unjust). This was stated explicitly by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi. And the author of al-Hidayah said: The statement is the judge's also in the correct view, because he attributes his action to a known state that negates guarantee, so it becomes like when a man says: 'I divorced or freed and I was insane' and the insanity was well-known among people, then his statement is accepted so that divorce and manumission do not occur due to his attributing to a state that negates the occurrence. If the cutter and taker (the ones who suffered the punishment) in this section confess to what the judge confessed, they become liable, because they confessed to a cause of guarantee. And the judge's statement is accepted in repelling the guarantee itself, not in nullifying it for others, unlike the first cause of guarantee because his action during his judgeship is established by mutual agreement. (Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah) 'Right': And the one against whom the ruling was made said: 'You did it unjustly.' (T) 'His action' meaning he did this action which is ruling regarding money in the first issue and cutting of hand in the second. (Ayni) 'While he was a judge' meaning in the state that he was a judge at that time. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage deals with the acceptance of a dismissed judge's statement regarding a previous ruling. The scenario: a judge who has been dismissed says to a man, 'I took a thousand dirhams from you and gave it to Zaid, and I ruled it against you as a right due to him.' The man responds, 'You took it unjustly.' The ruling: the judge's statement is accepted without oath, provided the man admits that the judge was still a judge when he did it. The same applies if the judge says he ruled to cut the man's hand. The commentary explains that the judge is not required to take an oath because if he did, he would become a litigant, and a litigant's judgment is not valid. The passage then categorizes judges into four types: (1) knowledgeable and just – his statement is accepted unconditionally; (2) just but ignorant – he must explain his ruling well to be believed; (3) ignorant and immoral or knowledgeable and immoral – his statement is not accepted unless witnesses are present or a just person testifies with him. Imam Muhammad's later view is that the judge's statement is not accepted unless he presents evidence, and many later scholars adopted this due to corruption among judges. However, the apparent riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) accepts the judge's statement because he reports what he has the authority to initiate and is not suspected in his report. The text also references al-Hidayah, which analogizes the situation to a man who says 'I divorced while insane'—his statement is accepted if his insanity is known.

Key Terms
قاض عزل (qāḍī 'azl): A judge who has been dismissed from office.
محمل ومفسر (muḥammal wa mufassar): In summary or in detail; the statement of a knowledgeable just judge is accepted whether he explains briefly or in detail.
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent/reliable transmission from the early Hanafi masters, as opposed to the nawadir (rare transmissions).

Key Takeaway
A dismissed judge's statement about his past ruling is accepted without oath if the affected party admits the act occurred while the judge was in office, reflecting trust in the judiciary's apparent integrity.

Classification of Judges and Acceptance of Their Statements
Classification of judges into four types and rule for accepting their statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of judges according to the Hanafi school and state the ruling on accepting each type's statement.

Core Idea
A judge's statement is accepted based on his knowledge and justice; a learned just judge's statement is accepted unconditionally.

In this passage, the Hanafi school classifies judges into four categories based on two attributes: knowledge ('ilm) and justice ('adālah). The ruling on accepting a judge's statement varies accordingly. We'll also examine an important later dispute within the school regarding the standard for accepting a judge's statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two attributes used to classify judges
Recognize that the classification is based on knowledge ('ilm) and justice ('adālah). Each attribute has two levels, yielding four combinations.
Knowledge refers to legal expertise; justice refers to moral uprightness.
2
List the four categories
Name the four types: knowledgeable just ('ālim 'ādil), knowledgeable unjust ('ālim fāsiq), ignorant just (jāhil 'ādil), and ignorant unjust (jāhil fāsiq).
3
For each category, state the ruling on accepting the judge's statement
The knowledgeable just judge's statement is accepted unconditionally (muḥammalan wa mufassaran). The ignorant just judge must explain; if he explains well, he is believed. The knowledgeable unjust and ignorant unjust judges are not believed unless they present the original evidence (yu‘āyinu sabab al-ḥukm).
Note the condition for the unjust judge: he must witness the cause of the ruling, i.e., the witnesses.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the older view (Zahir al-Riwayah) which accepts the just judge's statement, with Imam Muhammad's later opinion that the judge's statement is not accepted unless he produces evidence. Understand why many later scholars adopted Muhammad's view due to corruption.
The text notes that many mashāyikh adopted Muhammad's narration because of widespread corruption among judges.
5
Understand the practical effect
In later practice, due to corruption, the stricter view (Muhammad's) is often applied, meaning judges must produce evidence. However, the Zahir al-Riwayah position remains the basis for acceptance of a just judge's statement.
The exception for necessity (ḥājah) in accepting written judgments (kitāb) shows the tension between theory and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم القضاة أربعة : عالم عادل، وعالم جائر، وجاهل عادل وجاهل جائر، فيقبل قول الأول محملاً ومفسراً، وإن كان عادلاً جاهلاً يستفسر، فإن أحسن تفسيره وجب تصديقه، وإلا لا، وإن كان جاهلاً فاسقاً أو عالماً فاسقاً لا يقبل قوله إلا أن يعاين سبب الحكم، وهو الشهود، أو يشهد بذلك مع القاضي عدل في حق يثبت بشاهدين، ومعناه: أن يشهد القاضي والعدل على شهادة الذين شهدوا بسبب الحد، وقال محمد آخراً: لا يقبل قول القاضي حتى يعاين الحجة، وكثير من مشايخنا أخذوا برواية محمد في هذا؛ لفساد أكثر قضاة هذا الزمان لاسيما في قضاة البلاد الذين يتولون برشوة وهم في أنفسهم جهلاء، وأكثرهم فسقة وهذا يقتضي أن لا يقبل كتابه أيضاً إلا أنهم تركوا هذا القول في الكتاب للحاجة إليه، وجه ظاهر الرواية: أن القاضي أخبر عما يملك إنشائه، ومن تمكن من الإنشاء عما أخبر به لم يتهم في خبره، ولأن في تصديقه طاعة، فيجب تصديقه. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
Then the judges are four: a knowledgeable just one, a knowledgeable unjust one, an ignorant just one, and an ignorant unjust one. So the statement of the first (knowledgeable just) is accepted whether he explains in detail or in summary. And if he is just but ignorant, he is asked for explanation: if he explains well, he must be believed; otherwise not. And if he is ignorant and immoral or knowledgeable and immoral, his statement is not accepted unless he witnesses the cause of the ruling, which is the witnesses, or he testifies with the judge (when the judge is) just in a right that is proven by two witnesses. Its meaning is that the judge and the just person testify to the testimony of those who witnessed the cause of the hadd. And Muhammad said later: The judge's statement is not accepted until he witnesses the evidence. Many of our mashayikh adopted Muhammad's narration due to the corruption of most judges of this time, especially the judges of the regions who take bribes and are ignorant in themselves, and most of them are immoral. This necessitates that his letter should also not be accepted except that they abandoned this opinion in the book due to necessity. The rationale of the apparent riwayah is that the judge reports what he has the power to initiate, and one who has the power to initiate concerning what he reports is not accused in his report, and because believing him is obedience, so he must be believed. (Ayni, Fath, 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of judges into four categories based on knowledge ('ilm) and justice ('adalah). The first category is knowledgeable and just ('ālim 'ādil). His statement is accepted unconditionally, whether he provides a detailed explanation or a summary (muḥammal or mufassar). The second is just but ignorant (jāhil 'ādil). He must be asked for an explanation; if he explains well, his statement is believed; otherwise, it is not. The third and fourth are immoral (fāsiq) whether knowledgeable or ignorant). Their statements are not accepted unless they can present the original evidence (witnesses) or a just person testifies with the judge. The passage also notes Imam Muhammad's later opinion that the judge's statement is not accepted unless he produces evidence, and many later scholars (mashāyikh) adopted this view due to widespread corruption among judges. However, the apparent riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) accepts the judge's statement because he reports what he has the authority to initiate and is not suspected in his report. The practical effect is that the standard for accepting a judge's statement has been tightened in later practice due to corruption.

Key Terms
عالم عادل (‘ālim ‘ādil): A judge who is knowledgeable in Islamic law and just in his conduct.
محملاً ومفسراً (muḥammalan wa mufassaran): In summary (muḥammal) or in detail (mufassar); his statement is accepted without needing elaboration.
يعاين سبب الحكم (yu‘āyinu sabab al-ḥukm): He witnesses the basis of the ruling, i.e., the witnesses or evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of judge's statement is accepted unconditionally?
A) The knowledgeable unjust judge
B) The ignorant just judge
C) The knowledgeable just judge
D) The ignorant unjust judge

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies judges by knowledge and justice, and the acceptance of their statements varies; later scholars tightened the standard due to corruption.

The Weight of a Qadi's Word: Acceptance and Rejection in Hanafi Fiqh
Rulings on a qadi's statement and classification of qadis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for accepting a qadi's statement regarding his judgments and identify the four categories of qadis with their respective procedural treatment.

Core Idea
The qadi's word is accepted only when his character and tenure align with justice.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical question in judicial procedure: when can a qadi's own statement about a past judgment be taken as proof? The text lays out a nuanced classification of qadis and the conditions under which their testimony is accepted, reflecting the Hanafi school's realism about judicial integrity. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone involved in Islamic legal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial case
A former qadi claims he executed a judgment (e.g., took money or cut a hand). The opponent admits the act occurred but says it was unjust.
This sets the stage for the ruling: the qadi's word is accepted because the opponent confirms the act happened during his tenure.
2
Note the condition for acceptance
The opponent must admit that the act occurred while the qadi was in office. If the opponent denies the qadi was in office, the qadi's statement is not accepted.
This condition is crucial: the qadi's authority only covers acts done in his official capacity.
3
Classify the qadi into one of four types
The qadi's knowledge and justice ('ilm and 'adl) determine the rule. The four categories are: knowledgeable just, knowledgeable unjust, ignorant just, ignorant unjust.
The classification is based on two characteristics: knowledge ('ilm) and justice ('adalah).
4
Apply the corresponding rule
Only the knowledgeable just qadi is accepted without question. The ignorant just must explain; if he explains well, he is believed. The corrupt or ignorant qadi is only believed if the evidence (witnesses) is produced.
The rules become stricter with lack of knowledge or justice.
5
Recognise the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad later held that even a just qadi's statement is not accepted unless he can produce the evidence. Many later scholars adopted this due to corruption.
This dispute does not affect the four-category framework but adds a layer of procedural caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قال قاض عزل لرجل: أخذت منك ألفاً ودفعتها إلى زيد قضيت به عليك، بألف حق له عليك فقال الرجل: أخذته ظلما فالقول للقاضي، وكذا لو قال: قضيت بقطع يدك في حق أي الألف أي بطريق الظلم أي يصدق القاضي بلا يمين إذا كان المقطوع يده والمأخوذ منه المال مقراً أنه فعله وهو قاض. ثم القضاة أربعة : عالم عادل، وعالم جائر، وجاهل عادل وجاهل جائر، فيقبل قول الأول محملاً ومفسراً، وإن كان عادلاً جاهلاً يستفسر، فإن أحسن تفسيره وجب تصديقه، وإلا لا، وإن كان جاهلاً فاسقاً أو عالماً فاسقاً لا يقبل قوله إلا أن يعاين سبب الحكم، وهو الشهود، أو يشهد بذلك مع القاضي عدل في حق يثبت بشاهدين، ومعناه: أن يشهد القاضي والعدل على شهادة الذين شهدوا بسبب الحد، وقال محمد آخراً: لا يقبل قول القاضي حتى يعاين الحجة، وكثير من مشايخنا أخذوا برواية محمد في هذا؛ لفساد أكثر قضاة هذا الزمان لاسيما في قضاة البلاد الذين يتولون برشوة وهم في أنفسهم جهلاء، وأكثرهم فسقة وهذا يقتضي أن لا يقبل كتابه أيضاً إلا أنهم تركوا هذا القول في الكتاب للحاجة إليه، وجه ظاهر الرواية: أن القاضي أخبر عما يملك إنشائه، ومن تمكن من الإنشاء عما أخبر به لم يتهم في خبره، ولأن في تصديقه طاعة، فيجب تصديقه. (عيني، فتح، عناية) عزل : أي عن القضاء وهو صفة قاض. (معدن قضيت أي حال كونه قد قضيت. فالقول للقاضي: [أي بغير عين؛ لأنه ثبت أنه فعل ذلك في حال قضائه. (عيني)] لأن المقضي عليه لما أقر أنه فعله في قضائه كان الظاهر شاهداً للقاضي؛ إذ القاضي لا يقضي بالجور ظاهراً، ولا يمين على القاضي؛ لأنه لو لزمه يمين صار خصماً، وقضاء الخصم لا ينفذ، والحاصل أن القول للقاضي، ولا يلزمه الضمان إذا كان المأخوذ ماله والمقطوع يده مقراً بأنه فعل ذلك وهو قاض بالاتفاق، فعلم من هذا أن المقطوع يده والمأخوذ ماله إذا زعم أنه لم يكن قاضياً يومئذ، وإنما فعل ذلك قبل التقليد أو بعد العزل، كان القول قول المدعي، نص عليه شمس الأئمة السرخسي. : وقال صاحب "الهداية": القول للقاضي أيضاً في الصحيح؛ لأنه أسند فعله إلى حالة معهودة منافية للضمان، فصار كما إذا قال الرجل: طلقت أو أعتقت وأنا مجنون والجنون كان معلوماً بين الناس، فالقول قوله، حتى لا يقع الطلاق والعتاق؛ لإضافته إلى حالة منافية للإيقاع، ولو أقر القاطع والآخذ في هذا الفصل بما أقر به القاضي يضمنان؛ لأنهما أقرا بسبب الضمان، وقول القاضي مقبول في دفع الضمان نفسه، لا في إبطال عن عن غيره، بخلاف سبب الضمان الأول بأنه ثبت فعله في قضائه بالتصادق (عيني، فتح، عناية) حق: وقال المقضي عليه: فعلته ظلماً. (ط) كان ( عيني) فعله أي فعل هذا الفعل وهو الحكم بالمال في المسألة الأولى وقطع مقراً: انتصابه على أنه خبر اليد في الثانية. (عيني) وهو قاض أي والحال أنه قاض في ذلك الوقت. (عيني)
And if a qadi removed from office says to a man: 'I took from you a thousand dirhams and paid it to Zaid as a judgment against you for a right due to him,' and the man says: 'You took it unjustly,' then the statement is the qadi's. Similarly if he said: 'I judged the cutting of your hand for a right' - meaning the thousand dirhams, unjustly. That is, the qadi is believed without oath, provided that the one whose hand was cut and the one from whom the money was taken admit that he did that while he was a qadi. Then the qadis are four: a knowledgeable just one, a knowledgeable unjust one, an ignorant just one, and an ignorant unjust one. The statement of the first is accepted whether general or detailed. If he is just but ignorant, he is asked for explanation; if he explains well, his statement must be accepted, otherwise not. If he is ignorant and corrupt or knowledgeable and corrupt, his statement is not accepted unless the cause of the judgment (i.e., the witnesses) is witnessed, or a just person along with the qadi testifies to that in a case that requires two witnesses. The meaning is that the qadi and the just person testify to the testimony of those who testified on account of the prescribed punishment. And Muhammad said later: 'The qadi's statement is not accepted unless the evidence is witnessed.' Many of our teachers adopted the narration of Muhammad in this due to the corruption of most qadis of this time, especially the qadis of the provinces who take bribes and are themselves ignorant, and most of them corrupt. This would require that his letter also not be accepted, but they left this opinion in the book due to need. The apparent transmission's reasoning is that the qadi informs about what he has the power to create, and one who has the power to create what he informed about is not suspected in his information, and because obeying him is obedience, so he must be believed. (Ayni, Fath, 'Inaya) He said: 'You took it unjustly.'
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings related to the testimony of a qadi. The first ruling deals with a case where a deposed qadi claims he administered a judgment against someone. The qadi is believed because his act occurred during his tenure, and the opponent admits the act happened while he was a judge. The second ruling classifies qadis into four categories. Only a knowledgeable just qadi is accepted without elaboration. An ignorant just qadi is questioned; if he explains properly, he is believed. A corrupt or ignorant qadi is only believed if the evidence (like witnesses) is produced, or another just person testifies with him. Imam Muhammad later ruled that a qadi's statement is not accepted at all unless he witnessed the evidence; many later Hanafi scholars adopted this due to widespread corruption among qadis. The reasoning of the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) is that the qadi is reporting something he had authority to create, so he is not suspect, and his judgment entails obedience. The text then extends the rule: if the claimant of injury denies the qadi was in office at the time, the claimant's word is taken. The Hidayah adds that the qadi's word is accepted even in the sound view, likening it to a man who says he divorced while insane—his statement is accepted because he attributes the act to a state inconsistent with liability.

Key Terms
قاض (qadi): A judge appointed to adjudicate disputes according to Islamic law.
عزل ('azl): Removal from office as a qadi.
ظالم (zalim): Unjust, acting contrary to the law. Here used to describe a qadi who commits injustice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His statement is accepted unconditionally.
B) He is asked for an explanation.
C) His statement is not accepted unless the evidence (witnesses) is witnessed.
D) His statement is accepted only if he takes an oath.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a qadi's statement depends on his character and the presence of evidence, with later Hanafi scholars adopting a stricter stance due to judicial corruption.

Witness Correction Within the Judge's Council
States conditions for accepting a witness's correction before leaving the court

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi court accepts a witness's correction of testimony within the same session and apply the ruling to a case of a disputed amount.

Core Idea
A witness's correction is accepted only if made before leaving the judge's council, but the original testimony stands.

A witness may err due to the gravity of the court. Hanafi law allows him to correct his mistake while still in the judge's presence, provided he is just and the correction is made promptly. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq details the conditions and consequences of such a correction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a witness correcting his testimony by saying 'awhamtu' (I erred) or similar. The ruling is that this correction is accepted (taqbal) if conditions are met.
The correction is not a retraction but a clarification.
2
List the conditions for acceptance
Conditions: witness must be just (adl), must not have left the judge's council (lam yabrah), the session must not have been long, the plaintiff must not have denied the correction, and there must be no contradiction (e.g., attributing the right to another person).
These conditions ensure the correction is not due to external pressure.
3
Distinguish between 'place of doubt' and other matters
A 'place of doubt' (mawdi' al-shubha) involves a change in the quantity or value (e.g., amount of money). For non-doubt matters like mispronouncing a name, the witness can simply repeat the testimony without issue.
Only in place of doubt does the ruling become complex.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the enforced amount
Abu Hanifa holds that the original testimony (e.g., 1000 dirhams) is enforced because the right was already established. Al-Sarakhsi and Muhammad al-Shaybani incline toward the corrected amount (500). The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's.
The dispute hinges on whether the correction is treated as a new testimony or a mere clarification.
5
Apply to a concrete example
A just witness testifies '1000 dirhams', then immediately says 'I erred, it is 500 dirhams' while still in court. According to the primary view, the judge enforces 1000 dirhams. If the witness leaves court and then corrects, it is rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شهد ولم يبرح حتى قال أو همت بعض شهادتي، تقبل لو عدلاً. في مجلس القاضي أي أسقطت وتركت أي شهادته ويسمع قوله ولم يبرح: أي لم يزل عن مجلس القاضي و لم يطل المجلس و لم يكذبه المشهود له. (ط، عيني) أوهمت إلخ: وفي المعراج: أوهم في الحساب مائة أسقط ،وزنا، ومعنى، وأوهم من صلاته ركعة تركها، والمعنى أخطأت بذكر زيادة كانت باطلة أو أخطأت بنسيان ما كان يجب علي ذكره، ولو قال الشاهد: "شككت أو غلطت أو نسيت فهو مثل ،أو همت والتقييد بالبعض يفيد أنه لو قال: "أوهمت الحق إنما هو لفلان آخر" لم يقبل. (عيني، فتح، عناية) تقبل: مقيد بعدم طول المجلس، وعدم تكذيب المشهود له، وعدم المناقضة؛ لأن الشاهد قد يبتلى بالغلط؛ لمهابة مجلس القاضي، فوضح العذر ، فتقبل شهادته إذا تداركه في أوانه لو كان الشاهد عدلاً ثابت العدالة عند القاضي، وإن قال هذا القول بعد ما قام عن مجلس القاضي، لا تقبل شهادته؛ لجواز أن أحد الخصمين غره بالرشوة، وهذا موضع شبهة كالزيادة والنقصان في قدر المال، وإذا لم يكن موضع شبهة، فلا بأس بإعادة الكلام مثل أن لفظ الشهادة، أو اسم المدعي أو المدعى عليه، أو ترك الإشارة إلى أحد الخصمين، وما يجري مجراه، وإن قام عن المجلس بعد أن يكون عدلاً، وإنما يتصور ذلك قبل القضاء؛ لأن لفظ الشهادة وبيان اسم المتخاصمين والإشارة إليهما من شرط القضاء. إذا كان يدع . والحاصل: أن الشاهد إن كان غير عدل ترد شهادته مطلقاً، سواء قاله في المجلس أو بعده، وسواء كان في موضع الشبهة أو غيره، وإن كان عدلاً قبلت في غير موضع الشبهة، وإذا كان في موضع الشبهة كما إذا شهد بألف درهم تم قال: غلطت بل هي خمس مائة أو بالعكس، فإنها تقبل إذا قال في المجلس بجميع ما شهد به أولاً يعني يقضى بألف في المثال المذكور؛ لأن المشهود به أولاً صار حقاً للمدعي، ووجب على القاضي القضاء به، فلا يبطل برجوعه، وقيل: يقضي بما بقي؛ لأن الحادث بعد الشهادة قبل القضاء كالحادث عند الشهادة، وإليه مال شمس الأئمة السرخسي. (عيني، فتح، عناية)
Whoever testifies and has not left [the court] until he said: 'I erred in part of my testimony,' it is accepted if he is just. In the judge's council: i.e., I dropped and left. i.e., his testimony, and his statement is heard. 'And he has not left': i.e., he has not left the judge's council, and the session has not been long, and the one for whom he testified has not denied him. (T, Ayni) 'I erred' etc.: In al-Mi'raj: 'He erred in calculation of one hundred' meaning dropped, in weight and meaning, and 'He erred in his prayer by a rak'ah' meaning he omitted it, and the meaning is 'I made an error by mentioning an addition that was invalid, or I made an error by forgetting what I should have mentioned.' If the witness said: 'I doubted or I made a mistake or I forgot,' it is like 'I erred.' The restriction to 'some' indicates that if he said: 'I erred, the right belongs to someone else,' it is not accepted. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah) 'It is accepted': restricted by the session not being long, the one for whom he testified not denying him, and no contradiction; because the witness may be afflicted with error due to awe of the judge's council, so the excuse is clear, so his testimony is accepted if he rectifies it in its time, provided the witness is just, with confirmed justice in the judge's view. If he says this statement after he has left the judge's council, his testimony is not accepted; because it is possible that one of the litigants deceived him with bribe, and this is a place of doubt like increase and decrease in the amount of money. If it is not a place of doubt, there is no problem in repeating the speech, such as the wording of testimony, or the name of the plaintiff or defendant, or omitting pointing to one of the litigants, and things like that, even if he left the council after being just. And this can only be imagined before judgment; because the wording of testimony and stating the names of litigants and pointing to them are conditions of judgment. If he was ... (unclear). And the summary: The witness, if he is not just, his testimony is rejected absolutely, whether he said it in the council or after, whether it is in a place of doubt or otherwise. And if he is just, it is accepted in that which is not a place of doubt. And if it is a place of doubt, as when he testifies to a thousand dirhams then says: 'I made a mistake, rather it is five hundred' or vice versa, then it is accepted if he says it in the council concerning all of his initial testimony, meaning he is judged by the thousand in the mentioned example; because the initial testimony became a right for the plaintiff, and it became obligatory for the judge to judge by it, so it is not nullified by his retraction. And it is said: He is judged by what remains; because what happens after testimony before judgment is like what happens at the time of testimony. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi inclined to this. (Ayni, Fath, Inayah)
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the ruling on a witness who, while still in the judge's council after testifying, says that he made a mistake (awhamtu) in part of his testimony. The author, Imam Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, states the basic ruling: if the witness is just (adl), his correction is accepted, provided he has not left the court and the session has not been lengthy. The commentators (al-Ayni, Ibn al-Humam, and others) expand on the conditions. Key points: (1) The phrase 'awhamtu' means 'I erred'—whether by adding a false element or omitting a necessary part. Saying 'shakaktu' (I doubted) or 'ghalitu' (I made a mistake) has the same effect. (2) If the witness simply attributes the right to a different person, his retraction is not accepted because it contradicts his original testimony. (3) The acceptance of the correction is conditioned on: the witness being just; the court session not being long; the plaintiff not denying the correction; and the correction not contradicting the original testimony. (4) The reasoning is that awe of the court may cause the witness to err initially; thus his correction while still in court is trusted. If he leaves the court before correcting, his subsequent retraction is not accepted due to suspicion of bribery or undue influence. (5) The place of doubt (mawdi' shubha) refers to changes in the amount of money (e.g., from 1000 to 500). In such cases, if he corrects within the session, the original testimony (the larger amount) is upheld as per the stronger position (Abu Hanifa's view), because the right has already been established for the plaintiff. However, al-Sarakhsi preferred the view that the corrected amount (the smaller) is taken, as the new statement is like a new testimony. The relied-upon fatwa is that the original testimony stands. (6) For non-doubt matters (e.g., mispronunciation of names), the witness may simply repeat without issue. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
أوهمت (awhamtu): I made an error in testimony, either by adding something false or omitting something necessary.
لم يبرح (lam yabrah): He has not left the judge's council (majlis al-qada).
موضع الشبهة (mawdi' al-shubha): A matter where the testimony involves a change in the quantity or value (e.g., amount of money).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A witness testifies that the defendant owes 1,000 dirhams, then immediately says, 'I made a mistake; it is 500 dirhams.' He is a just witness and has not left the court. According to the primary Hanafi position, what is the judgment?
A) The witness's correction is rejected entirely.
B) The judge enforces the original testimony of 1,000 dirhams.
C) The judge enforces the corrected amount of 500 dirhams.
D) The judge dismisses the case because of inconsistency.

Key Takeaway
A witness's correction of testimony is accepted only if made within the judge's council and under specific conditions, but the original amount is enforced in matters of disputed quantity.

The Ten Aspects of Correspondence between Testimony and Claim
Ruling on the requirement of correspondence between testimony and claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ten aspects in which testimony must agree with the claim and apply the rule to evaluate whether a given testimony matches the claim.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted only if it matches the claim in ten aspects; otherwise it is rejected as contradictory.

Testimony serves to confirm the plaintiff's claim. If it contradicts the claim in any fundamental aspect, it defeats its purpose and cannot be the basis for judgment. The Hanafi school has enumerated ten categories where this agreement is required, including type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, passive action, position, ownership, and relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
The passage opens by stating that testimony is accepted if it agrees with the claim, otherwise not. This is the central principle. Agreement is required in meaning, not necessarily in wording.
2
List the ten aspects
From the passage, extract the ten categories: النوع (type), الكم (quantity), الكيف (quality), الزمان (time), المكان (place), الفعل (action), الانفعال (passive action), الوضع (position), الملك (ownership), النسبة (relationship).
These are exhaustive for Hanafi law.
3
Understand the rationale
Testimony that contradicts the claim belies it. In rights of humans, a valid claim is a precondition. The judge can only rule if the evidence supports the claim. In rights of Allah, a claim is not required.
Exception: hudud cases need no prior claim.
4
Apply the rule with examples
The passage gives examples: claiming 10 dinars and testifying 10 dirhams (type mismatch), claiming red garment and testifying white (quality mismatch), etc. Check if the student can correctly classify each discrepancy.
A single mismatch in any aspect makes testimony invalid.
5
Distinguish rights of Allah vs. humans
In rights of Allah (e.g., hadd crimes), the testimony may be accepted without a claim. For rights of humans, a claim must precede. This is a key Hanafi distinction.
Other schools may not make this distinction.

باب الاختلاف في الشهادة أي في بيان أحكامه الشهادة إن وافقت الدعوى قبلت وإلا لا . ادّعى دارا. أي لا تقبل رجل على آخر باب: لما ذكر مسائل الاتفاق وهو الأصل، شرع في مسائل ،الاختلاف ومبنى الباب على أصول: منها: أن الشهادة على حقوق العباد لا تقبل بلا دعوى بخلاف حقوقه تعالى ومنها : أن الشهادة بأكثر من المدعى باطلة، بخلاف الأقل؛ للاتفاق فيه ومنها أن الملك المطلق أزيد من المقيد؛ لثبوته من الأصل، والملك بالسبب مقتصر على وقت السبب، ومنها: موافقة الشهادتين لفظاً ، ومعنى، وموافقة الشهادة الدعوى معنى فقط. (عيني، فتح، عناية) قبلت : أي الشهادة؛ لأنها طابقت الدعوى فأمكن قضاء القاضي بها (عيني) وإلا لا : [ أي وإن لم يوافق الشهادة الدعوى بأن كانت بألف قرض وشهدا بألف ثمن متاع (عيني)] أي وإن لم يوافق الشهادة الدعوى لا تقبل؛ لأنها خالفت الدعوى، فلم يمكن القضاء بها؛ وذلك لأن الشهادة لأجل تصديق الدعوى، فإذا خالفتها فقد كذبتها، والدعوى الكاذبة لا تعتبر، فانعدم الشرط، وهو تقدم تصديق الدعوى، فلا يحكم بها ، بخلاف حقوق الله تعالى؛ لأن الدعوى ليست فيها بشرط [ رمز الحقائق: ١٥٢/٢] ادعى داراً وكذا لو ادعى ديناً بقرض فشهدا بملك مطلق. (فتح)
Chapter on difference in testimony: i.e., regarding explanation of its rulings. Testimony, if it agrees with the claim, is accepted; otherwise not. He claimed a house. i.e., It is not accepted [from] a man against another. Chapter: After mentioning matters of agreement, which is the foundation, he began matters of difference. The basis of the chapter rests on principles: Among them: Testimony concerning rights of servants (humans) is not accepted without a claim, unlike rights of Allah Almighty. Among them: Testimony for more than what is claimed is invalid, unlike less; due to agreement on that. Among them: Absolute ownership is greater than restricted ownership; because it is proven from the origin, and ownership by cause is limited to the time of the cause. Among them: Agreement of two testimonies in wording and meaning, and agreement of testimony with claim in meaning only. (Fath) 'Difference' includes violation of testimony from the claim, difference between two witnesses, and difference between two groups. (Fath) 'Testimony' [i.e., whether it agrees with the claim or what is testified is less. (Fath)] You already know the meaning of testimony. Claim: It is a demand of a right in the council of one who has authority to resolve when it is proven. The meaning of their agreement: That the claim and testimony be united in ten things: type, quantity, quality, time, place, action, passive action, position, ownership, and relationship. If the testimony violates in any of these things, it is not in agreement with the claim. For example: If he claimed against another ten dinars and the witness testified to ten dirhams—in type; or claimed nine dirhams and testified to fifteen—in quantity; or claimed theft of a red garment and testified to a white one—in quality; or claimed killing of his relative on the Day of Sacrifice in Kufa, and testified to that on the Day of Breaking the Fast in Basra—in time and place; or claimed splitting his water-skin and destruction of what was in it by splitting, and testified to its splitting in his presence—in action and passive action; or claimed real estate on the eastern side of the property of so-and-so, and testified to the western side of it—in position; or claimed that it was his property and testified that it was the property of his son—in ownership; or claimed that he was his slave born from such-and-such slave girl, and testified to birth from another—in relationship; in all these cases the testimony is not in agreement with the claim. And in His statement: 'If it agrees with the claim' is an indication that the precedence of the claim in rights of humans is a condition for acceptance of testimony. So it is accepted in what agrees with the claim; because it is possible for the judge to judge by it. As for agreement in their wording, it is not a condition. Do you not see that the plaintiff says: 'I claim against my debtor this' and the witness says: 'I testify to that'? (Ayni, Fath, Inayah) 'Accepted': i.e., the testimony, because it matched the claim, so the judge can judge by it. (Ayni) 'Otherwise not': [i.e., if the testimony does not agree with the claim, such as if it was for a loan of a thousand and they testified for a thousand as price of goods (Ayni)] i.e., if the testimony does not agree with the claim, it is not accepted; because it violated the claim, so judgment cannot be made by it. And that is because testimony is for the purpose of verifying the claim. So if it violates it, it has belied it, and a false claim is not considered. So the condition is absent, which is the precedence of verifying the claim. Therefore, judgment is not made by it, unlike the rights of Allah Almighty, because a claim is not a condition in them. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 2/152] He claimed a house. Similarly, if he claimed a debt by loan and they testified to absolute ownership. (Fath)
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq begins the chapter on differences in testimony. The core ruling is that testimony is accepted only if it conforms to the claim (da'wa). The author then explains the principles behind this rule. Testimony serves to verify the plaintiff's claim; if it contradicts the claim, it effectively falsifies it, and thus cannot be the basis for judgment. In rights of Allah (hudud, etc.), a claim is not a prerequisite, but in rights of humans, a valid claim must precede. The commentator (Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir) elaborates on the ten aspects in which testimony must agree with the claim: type (e.g., dinars vs. dirhams), quantity (e.g., 9 vs. 15), quality (red vs. white), time (Day of Sacrifice vs. Day of Breaking Fast), place (Kufa vs. Basra), action and passive action (active splitting vs. passive splitting), position (east side vs. west side), ownership (his ownership vs. his son's), and relationship (from this slave girl vs. another). If any of these differ, the testimony is not accepted. However, the agreement is only required in meaning, not in exact wording. For example, the plaintiff may say 'I claim against my debtor' and the witness says 'I testify to that' without repeating the exact phrasing. This is sufficient. Additionally, if the testimony is for less than what is claimed (e.g., claim of 10 dirhams, testimony of 5), it is accepted because it does not contradict the claim; but if it is for more (claim 10, testify 15), it is invalid because it exceeds the claim. Also, absolute ownership (milk mutlaq) is considered greater than restricted ownership (milk bi al-sabab), so if the claim is for a specific cause (e.g., loan), and the witness testifies to absolute ownership without mentioning the cause, it may not match. The relied-upon position is that testimony must match in the ten aspects; otherwise it is rejected. This principle is Zahir al-Riwayah and mufta bihi.

Key Terms
الدعوى (al-da'wa): A demand of a right made in the court of a judge who has authority to resolve it when proven.
موافقة الشهادة للدعوى (muwafaqat al-shahada li al-da'wa): Testimony must agree with the claim in meaning, not necessarily in wording, across ten specific categories.
الملك المطلق (al-milk al-mutlaq): Absolute ownership without specifying a cause, considered more comprehensive than restricted ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A plaintiff claims that the defendant stole a red camel. The witness testifies that the defendant stole a white camel. According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the status of the testimony?
A) The testimony is accepted because the type is the same (camel).
B) The testimony is accepted only if the witness corrects his statement.
C) The testimony is rejected because it differs in quality (color).
D) The judge may accept it at his discretion.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected if it contradicts the claim in any of the ten aspects; the agreement is in meaning, not wording.

Two Joint Agents: No Independent Action Except in Litigation
Hanafi rule on joint agency with litigation exception and intra-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on joint agency, identify the exception for litigation, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute regarding whether both agents must speak in court.

Core Idea
Two agents appointed together must act jointly—except in litigation, where one may represent the principal alone.

Joint agency (wakalah mushtaraka) requires both agents to act together, but Hanafi fiqh recognizes a practical exception for court proceedings. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the general rule and its conditions, then focuses on the dispute within the school: must both agents speak in court? Understanding this ruling clarifies how the principal's intent is balanced against the realities of litigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its condition
Locate the base ruling: two agents appointed with one statement may not act independently. Note key condition: the appointment must be in a single statement (كلام واحد).
If appointed with two separate statements, each may act alone.
2
Identify the exception: litigation
Find the exception 'illa fi khusumah' – only in litigation may one agent act alone. The author then explains why: simultaneous speech causes confusion in court.
The opinion needed can be obtained before court.
3
Locate the intra-madhhab dispute
Identify the opposing view: Zufar and the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) require both agents to speak because the principal relied on both opinions.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
4
Analyze the opposing proofs
Understand each side's dalil. The majority (jumhur) argue necessity to avoid confusion; the opposition argue the principal's reliance on joint judgment.
Note how the author uses 'لنا' (our proof) to present the majority view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Recognize that the majority position (one agent may speak alone) is the relied-upon view. Note the important caveat: prior consultation is required; otherwise even the majority invalidates the act.
The passage ends with 'إذا لم يشركه في الرأي' – failure to consult invalidates even for the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتصرف أحد الوكيلين وحده إلا في خصومة. هذا إذا وكلهما بكلام واحد بأن قال: وكلتكما ببيع عبدي هذا وبخلع امرأتي هذه. وأما إذا وكلهما بكلامين كان لكل واحد منهما أن يتفرد في التصرف. وشمل إطلاقه ما إذا كان أحدهما حراً بالغاً عاقلاً والآخر عبداً أو صبياً محجوراً عليه، وشمل ما إذا مات أحدهما أو ذهب عقله لم يجز للآخر أن يتصرف وحده. والوصاية والمضاربة والقضاء والتولية على الوقف كالوكالة، فليس لأحدهما الانفراد إلا في مسألة شرط الواقف النظر أو الاستبدال له مع فلان، فإن للواقف الانفراد دون فلان. أي لا يتصرف أحد الوكيلين بإنفراده فيما يحتاج فيه إلى الرأي إلا في خصومة؛ فإن تكلمهما فيها ليس بشرط عند الجمهور، ويجوز تكلم أحدهما. وقال زفر: يشترط تكلمهما؛ لأنه محتاج إلى الرأي والموكل لم يرض برأي أحدهما بدون الآخر، وبه قالت الثلاثة. ولنا أن اجتماعهما في التكلم يؤدي إلى التعسف والتشويش والتوحش في مجلس القضاء، والرأي يحتاج إليه قبل مجلس القضاء لتقديم الخصومة واستنباط ما هو الأصوب فيباشر أحدهما برأي تر، حتى لو باشر أحدهما بدون رأي الآخر لا يجوز عندنا أيضاً. وليس في كلامه ما يعين يشترط حضور رأيه عند الخصومة؛ لأن ذلك ليس بشرط عند عامتهم، فيحمل على ما هو الأعم منه ومن كونه سابقاً على الخصومة.
Neither of the two agents may act alone except in litigation. This is when they are appointed with one statement...
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage deals with joint agency: when two people are appointed as agents together in a single statement (e.g., 'I appoint both of you to sell my slave'), neither may act independently. However, if they are appointed in two separate statements, each may act alone. Exceptions include the case of a waqf where the founder stipulates independence. The major exception is litigation (khousouma): one of the two agents may represent the principal in court alone. This is the Hanafi position (the majority of the school). Zufar and the three (likely Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held that both must speak in court because the principal relied on both opinions. The majority retorts that having both speak causes confusion; the necessary consultation can occur before court. However, if the acting agent does not consult the other's opinion beforehand, it is invalid even according to the majority.

Key Terms
الوكيلان (al-wakilan): Two agents appointed jointly in a single appointment.
الخصومة (al-khusumah): Litigation, court case.
الثلاثة (al-thalaatha): In this context, refers to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the three leading Hanafi imams).
الجمهور (al-jumhur): The majority of Hanafi scholars (as opposed to the three and Zufar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two agents are appointed together with one statement, in which case can one of them act alone?
A) In any matter requiring opinion.
B) Only in litigation.
C) Never; both must always act together.
D) In all financial transactions.

Key Takeaway
Two agents appointed jointly must act together in all matters except litigation, where one may act alone provided he has consulted the other's opinion beforehand.
